style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">\n<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">Article 4.\xc2\xb0 of the General Law of Linguistic Rights of the Indigenous Peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>\n<li value="2"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_engfactobox"><b><a href="#ref_engfactobox">^</a></b></span> Spanish is the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> official language of the Mexican federal government.</li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Mexico</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>M\xc3\xa9xico</i></span>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[\xcb\x88mexiko]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-mx-M%C3%A9xico.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Es-mx-M%C3%A9xico.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-mx-M\xc3\xa9xico.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>), officially the <b>United Mexican States</b> (Spanish: <span lang="es"><i>Estados Unidos Mexicanos</i></span>, <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-mx-Estados_Unidos_Mexicanos.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/Es-mx-Estados_Unidos_Mexicanos.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-mx-Estados Unidos Mexicanos.ogg">listen</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>\xc2\xb7<a href="/wiki/File:Es-mx-Estados_Unidos_Mexicanos.ogg" title="File:Es-mx-Estados Unidos Mexicanos.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-presidencia.gob.mx_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presidencia.gob.mx-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-13">[13]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal republic</a> in the southern portion of North America. It is <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Mexico" title="Borders of Mexico">bordered</a> to the north by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>; to the south and west by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>; to the southeast by <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>; and to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Covering almost two million square kilometers (over 760,000&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-13">[13]</a></sup> Mexico is the sixth largest country in the Americas by total area and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by area">13th largest independent nation</a> in the world.</p>\n<p>With an estimated population of over 120 million,<sup id="cite_ref-INEGI_2010_Census_Statistics_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INEGI_2010_Census_Statistics-15">[15]</a></sup> Mexico is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">eleventh most populous</a> country and the <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone#Hispanosphere" title="Hispanophone">most populous Spanish-speaking</a> country in the world while being the second most populous country in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>. Mexico is a federation comprising 31 <a href="/wiki/States_of_Mexico" title="States of Mexico">states</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">special federal entity</a> that is also its capital and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Mexico#Largest_cities" title="List of cities in Mexico">most populous city</a>. Other <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas_of_Mexico" title="Metropolitan areas of Mexico">metropolises</a> include <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara_Metropolitan_Area" title="Guadalajara Metropolitan Area">Guadalajara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Guanajuato" title="Le\xc3\xb3n, Guanajuato">Le\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monterrey_Metropolitan_area" title="Monterrey Metropolitan area">Monterrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area_of_Puebla" title="Metropolitan area of Puebla">Puebla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Toluca" title="Greater Toluca">Toluca</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tijuana_metropolitan_area" title="Tijuana metropolitan area">Tijuana</a>.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_Mexico" title="Pre-Columbian Mexico">Pre-Columbian Mexico</a> was home to many advanced <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerican</a> civilizations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">Olmec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">Toltec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_civilization" title="Zapotec civilization">Zapotec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztec</a> before first contact with <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europeans</a>. In 1521, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">conquered and colonized</a> the territory from its base in <a href="/wiki/Mexico-Tenochtitlan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexico-Tenochtitlan">Mexico-Tenochtitlan</a>, which was administered as the <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">viceroyalty of New Spain</a>. Three centuries later, this territory became Mexico following recognition in 1821 after the colony\'s <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a>. The tumultuous post-independence period was characterized by <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Mexico#Independence" title="Economic history of Mexico">economic instability</a> and many political changes. The <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican\xe2\x80\x93American War">Mexican\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> (1846\xe2\x80\x9348) led to the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Mexico" title="Territorial evolution of Mexico">territorial cession</a> of the extensive northern territories to the United States. The <a href="/wiki/Pastry_War" title="Pastry War">Pastry War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Mexican_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Mexican War">Franco-Mexican War</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Reform_War" title="Reform War">civil war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Mexico" title="Emperor of Mexico">two empires</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Mexico#Porfiriato" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Mexico">a domestic dictatorship</a> occurred through the 19th century. The dictatorship was overthrown in the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a> of 1910, which culminated with the promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico" title="Constitution of Mexico">1917 Constitution</a> and the emergence of the country\'s current <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Mexico" title="Politics of Mexico">political system</a>.</p>\n<p>Mexico has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">fifteenth largest</a> nominal GDP and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">eleventh largest</a> by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mexico" title="Economy of Mexico">Mexican economy</a> is strongly linked to those of its <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA) partners, especially the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Mexico was the first <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American</a> member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD), joining in 1994. It is classified as an upper-middle income country by the World Bank<sup id="cite_ref-wb-upper-middle_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-upper-middle-18">[18]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Newly_industrialized_country" title="Newly industrialized country">newly industrialized country</a> by several analysts.<sup id="cite_ref-Globalization_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globalization-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Limits_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Limits-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AIA_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Principles_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Principles-22">[22]</a></sup> By 2050, Mexico could become the world\'s fifth or seventh largest economy.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The country is considered both a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and is often identified as an <a href="/wiki/Emerging_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Emerging Powers">emerging global power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Due to its rich culture and history, Mexico ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Mexico" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Mexico">first in the Americas and seventh in the world</a> by number of <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Mexico is a <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse country</a>, ranking fourth in the world by biodiversity. In 2016 it was the eighth most visited country in the world, with 35 million international arrivals.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Mexico is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G20</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Uniting_for_Consensus" title="Uniting for Consensus">Uniting for Consensus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Alliance" title="Pacific Alliance">Pacific Alliance</a>.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>\n<li href="#Pre-Columbian_Mexico"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Pre-Columbian Mexico</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Conquest_of_the_Aztec_Triple_Alliance_.281519.E2.80.931521.29"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Conquest of the Aztec Triple Alliance (1519\xe2\x80\x931521)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain_.281521.E2.80.931821.29"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Viceroyalty of New Spain (1521\xe2\x80\x931821)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#War_of_Independence_.281810.E2.80.931821.29"><span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Second_Republic_and_Second_Empire_.281846.E2.80.931867.29"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext">Second Republic and Second Empire (1846\xe2\x80\x931867)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Porfiriato_.281876.E2.80.931911.29"><span class="tocnumber">2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Porfiriato (1876\xe2\x80\x931911)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Mexican_Revolution_and_one-party_rule_.281910.E2.80.932000.29"><span class="tocnumber">2.8</span> <span class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Crime"><span class="tocnumber">4.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Crime</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Energy"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Energy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a sanitation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Ethnicity_and_race"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ethnicity and race</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-33"><a areas</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Women"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Women</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Visual_arts"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Visual arts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Cinema"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cinema</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-45"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">7.7</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Mexico" title="Name of Mexico">Name of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CodexMendoza01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/CodexMendoza01.jpg/220px-CodexMendoza01.jpg" width="220" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/CodexMendoza01.jpg/330px-CodexMendoza01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/CodexMendoza01.jpg/440px-CodexMendoza01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="622" data-file-height="735" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CodexMendoza01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDepiction of the founding myth of <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Mexico-Tenochtitlan</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Mendoza" title="Codex Mendoza">Codex Mendoza</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Name_of_Mexico" title="Name of Mexico">M\xc4\x93xihco</a></i> is the <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a> term for the heartland of the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztec Empire</a>, namely,<sup id="cite_ref-Bright2004_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bright2004-34">[34]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Mexico" title="Valley of Mexico">Valley of Mexico</a>, and its people, the <a href="/wiki/Mexica" title="Mexica">Mexica</a>, and surrounding territories. This became the future <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a> as a division of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> prior to independence (compare <i><a href="/wiki/Latium" title="Latium">Latium</a></i>). It is generally considered to be a <a href="/wiki/Toponym" class="mw-redirect" title="Toponym">toponym</a> for the valley which became the primary <a href="/wiki/Ethnonym" title="Ethnonym">ethnonym</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Triple_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Aztec Triple Alliance">Aztec Triple Alliance</a> as a result, or vice versa. After New Spain won independence from Spain, representatives decided to name the new country after its capital, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>. This was founded in 1524 on top of the ancient Mexica capital of <a href="/wiki/Mexico-Tenochtitlan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexico-Tenochtitlan">Mexico-Tenochtitlan</a>.</p>\n<p>Traditionally, the name Tenochtitlan was thought to come from <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a> <i>tetl</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Nahuatl" title="Help:IPA/Nahuatl">[\xcb\x88tet\xc9\xac]</a></span> ("rock") and <i>n\xc5\x8dchtli</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Nahuatl" title="Help:IPA/Nahuatl">[\xcb\x88no\xcb\x90t\xca\x83t\xc9\xaci]</a></span> ("<a href="/wiki/Opuntia" title="Opuntia">prickly pear</a>") and is often thought to mean "Among the prickly pears [growing among] rocks". However, one attestation in the late 16th-century manuscript known as "the Bancroft dialogues" suggests the second vowel was short, so that the true etymology remains uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The suffix <i>-co</i> is the Nahuatl <a href="/wiki/Locative" class="mw-redirect" title="Locative">locative</a>, making the word a place name. Beyond that, the etymology is uncertain. It has been suggested that it is derived from <a href="/wiki/Mextli" class="mw-redirect" title="Mextli">Mextli</a> or M\xc4\x93xihtli, a secret name for the god of war and patron of the Mexica, <a href="/wiki/Huitzilopochtli" title="Huitzilopochtli">Huitzilopochtli</a>, in which case M\xc4\x93xihco means "Place where Huitzilopochtli lives".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Another hypothesis suggests that <i>M\xc4\x93xihco</i> derives from a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of the Nahuatl words for "Moon" (<i>M\xc4\x93tztli</i>) and navel (<i>x\xc4\xabctli</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-edomex_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edomex-37">[37]</a></sup> This meaning ("Place at the Center of the Moon") might refer to Tenochtitlan\'s position in the middle of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Texcoco" title="Lake Texcoco">Lake Texcoco</a>. The system of interconnected lakes, of which Texcoco formed the center, had the form of a rabbit, which the Mesoamericans <a href="/wiki/Pareidolia" title="Pareidolia">pareidolically</a> associated with the <a href="/wiki/Moon_rabbit" title="Moon rabbit">Moon</a>. Still another hypothesis suggests that the word is derived from M\xc4\x93ctli, the goddess of <a href="/wiki/Agave_americana" title="Agave americana">maguey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-edomex_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edomex-37">[37]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The name of the city-state was transliterated to Spanish as M\xc3\xa9xico with the phonetic value of the letter \'x\' in Medieval Spanish, which represented the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">voiceless postalveolar fricative</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x83]</span>. This sound, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_fricative" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced postalveolar fricative">voiced postalveolar fricative</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x92]</span>, represented by a \'j\', evolved into a <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">voiceless velar fricative</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[x]</span> during the 16th century. This led to the use of the variant M\xc3\xa9jico in many publications in Spanish, most notably in Spain, whereas in Mexico and most other Spanish\xe2\x80\x93speaking countries M\xc3\xa9xico was the preferred spelling. In recent years the <a href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Espa\xc3\xb1ola">Real Academia Espa\xc3\xb1ola</a>, which regulates the Spanish language, determined that both variants are acceptable in Spanish but that the normative recommended <a href="/wiki/Spelling" title="Spelling">spelling</a> is M\xc3\xa9xico.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The majority of publications in all Spanish-speaking countries now adhere to the new norm, even though the alternative variant is still occasionally used.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Source cited formerly does not support the assertion (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, the \'x\' in Mexico represents neither the original nor the current sound, but the consonant cluster <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ks]</span>.</p>\n<p>The official name of the country has changed as the <a href="/wiki/Form_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Form of government">form of government</a> has changed. The declaration of independence signed on November 6, 1813 by the deputies of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_An%C3%A1huac" class="mw-redirect" title="Congress of An\xc3\xa1huac">Congress of An\xc3\xa1huac</a> called the territory <i><a href="/wiki/Solemn_Act_of_the_Declaration_of_Independence_of_Northern_America" title="Solemn Act of the Declaration of Independence of Northern America">Am\xc3\xa9rica Septentrional</a></i> (Northern America). On two occasions (1821\xe2\x80\x931823 and 1863\xe2\x80\x931867), the country was known as <span lang="es">Imperio Mexicano</span> (<a href="/wiki/Mexican_Empire_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Mexican Empire (disambiguation)">Mexican Empire</a>). All three federal constitutions (1824, 1857 and 1917, the current constitution) used the name <span lang="es">Estados Unidos Mexicanos</span><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94or the variant <span lang="es">Estados-Unidos Mexicanos</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> all of which have been translated as "United Mexican States". The phrase <span lang="es">Rep\xc3\xbablica Mexicana</span>, "Mexican Republic", was used in the 1836 Constitutional Laws.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mexico" title="History of Mexico">History of Mexico</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Roman_Catholicism_in_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Roman Catholicism in Mexico">History of Roman Catholicism in Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Mexico" title="Economic history of Mexico">Economic history of Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mexico_City" title="History of Mexico City">History of Mexico City</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_Mexico">Pre-Columbian Mexico</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_Mexico" title="Pre-Columbian Mexico">Pre-Columbian Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_chronology" title="Mesoamerican chronology">Mesoamerican chronology</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg/220px-15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg/330px-15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg/440px-15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5641" data-file-height="3766" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15-07-13-Teotihuacan-RalfR-WMA_0257.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nView of the <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_of_the_Moon" title="Pyramid of the Moon">Pyramid of the Moon</a> and entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Quetzalpap%C3%A1lotl_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Quetzalpap\xc3\xa1lotl Palace">Quetzalpap\xc3\xa1lotl Palace</a>. During its peak in the Classic era, <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a> dominated the Valley of Mexico and exerted political and cultural influence in other areas, such <a href="/wiki/Spearthrower_Owl" title="Spearthrower Owl">as in the Pet\xc3\xa9n Basin</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The earliest <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human</a> artifacts in Mexico are chips of <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">stone tools</a> found near campfire remains in the Valley of Mexico and radiocarbon-dated to circa 10,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-Werner2001_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Werner2001-42">[42]</a></sup> Mexico is the site of the domestication of maize, tomato and <a href="/wiki/Phaseolus" title="Phaseolus">beans</a>, which produced an agricultural surplus. This enabled the transition from <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">paleo-Indian</a> hunter-gatherers to sedentary agricultural villages beginning around 5000 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-EvansWebster2013_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EvansWebster2013-43">[43]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the subsequent formative eras, maize cultivation and cultural traits such as a mythological and religious complex, and a <a href="/wiki/Vigesimal" title="Vigesimal">vigesimal</a> numeric system, were diffused from the Mexican cultures to the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerican</a> culture area.<sup id="cite_ref-MacLachlan_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacLachlan-44">[44]</a></sup> In this period, villages became more dense in terms of population, becoming socially stratified with an artisan class, and developing into <a href="/wiki/Chiefdom" title="Chiefdom">chiefdoms</a>. The most powerful rulers had religious and political power, organizing construction of large ceremonial centers developed.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The earliest complex civilization in Mexico was the <a href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">Olmec</a> culture, which flourished on the Gulf Coast from around 1500 BCE. Olmec cultural traits diffused through Mexico into other formative-era cultures in Chiapas, Oaxaca and the Valley of Mexico. The formative period saw the spread of distinct religious and symbolic traditions, as well as artistic and architectural complexes.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The formative-era of Mesoamerica is considered one of the six independent <a href="/wiki/Cradles_of_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Cradles of civilization">cradles of civilization</a>.</p>\n<p>In the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_chronology" title="Mesoamerican chronology">pre-classical period</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_civilization" title="Zapotec civilization">Zapotec</a> civilizations developed complex centers at <a href="/wiki/Calakmul" title="Calakmul">Calakmul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monte_Alb%C3%A1n" title="Monte Alb\xc3\xa1n">Monte Alb\xc3\xa1n</a>, respectively. During this period the first true <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_writing_systems" title="Mesoamerican writing systems">Mesoamerican writing systems</a> were developed in the <a href="/wiki/Epi-Olmec_culture" title="Epi-Olmec culture">Epi-Olmec</a> and the Zapotec cultures. The Mesoamerican writing tradition reached its height in the Classic <a href="/wiki/Maya_Script" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya Script">Maya Hieroglyphic script</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In Central Mexico, the height of the classic period saw the ascendancy of <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a>, which formed a military and commercial empire whose political influence stretched south into the Maya area as well as north. Teotihuacan, with a population of more than 150,000 people, had some of the largest <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_pyramid" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesoamerican pyramid">pyramidal structures</a> in the pre-Columbian Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> After the collapse of Teotihuac\xc3\xa1n around 600 CE, competition ensued between several important political centers in central Mexico such as <a href="/wiki/Xochicalco" title="Xochicalco">Xochicalco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cholula_(Mesoamerican_site)" title="Cholula (Mesoamerican site)">Cholula</a>. At this time, during the Epi-Classic, <a href="/wiki/Nahua_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahua people">Nahua peoples</a> began moving south into Mesoamerica from the North, and became politically and culturally dominant in central Mexico, as they displaced speakers of <a href="/wiki/Oto-Manguean_languages" title="Oto-Manguean languages">Oto-Manguean languages</a>.</p>\n<dl>\n<dt>Post-classic period (ca. 1000\xe2\x80\x931519 AD)</dt>\n</dl>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg/220px-Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg/330px-Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg/440px-Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Murales_Rivera_-_Markt_in_Tlatelolco_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMural by Diego Rivera depicting the view from the <a href="/wiki/Tlatelolco_(altepetl)" title="Tlatelolco (altepetl)">Tlatelolco</a> markets into <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Mexico-Tenochtitlan</a>, one of the largest cities in the world at the time</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>During the early post-classic, Central Mexico was dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">Toltec</a> culture, <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Mixtec_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixtec civilization">Mixtec</a>, and the lowland Maya area had important centers at <a href="/wiki/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Chich\xc3\xa9n Itz\xc3\xa1">Chich\xc3\xa9n Itz\xc3\xa1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayap%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayap\xc3\xa1n">Mayap\xc3\xa1n</a>. Toward the end of the post-Classic period, the Mexica established dominance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a> originated the modern usage of "<a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztec</a>" as a collective term applied to all the people linked by trade, custom, religion, and language to the <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Mexica state</a> and \xc4\x92xc\xc4\x81n Tlaht\xc5\x8dl\xc5\x8dy\xc4\x81n, the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Triple Alliance</a>. In 1843, with the publication of the work of William H. Prescott, it was adopted by most of the world, including 19th-century Mexican scholars who considered it a way to distinguish present-day Mexicans from pre-conquest Mexicans. This usage has been the subject of debate since the late 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Port_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Port-49">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Aztec empire was an informal or hegemonic empire because it did not exert supreme authority over the conquered lands; it was satisfied with the payment of tributes from them. It was a discontinuous empire because not all dominated territories were connected; for example, the southern peripheral zones of <a href="/wiki/Soconusco" title="Soconusco">Xoconochco</a> were not in direct contact with the center. The hegemonic nature of the Aztec empire was demonstrated by their restoration of local rulers to their former position after their city-state was conquered. The Aztec did not interfere in local affairs, as long as the tributes were paid.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Aztec of Central Mexico built a tributary empire covering most of central Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_sacrifice_in_Aztec_culture" title="Human sacrifice in Aztec culture">The Aztec were noted for practicing human sacrifice</a> on a large scale. Along with this practice, they avoided killing enemies on the battlefield. Their warring casualty rate was far lower than that of their Spanish counterparts, whose principal objective was immediate slaughter during battle.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> This distinct Mesoamerican cultural tradition of human sacrifice ended with the Spanish conquest in the 16th century. Over the next centuries Mexican indigenous cultures were gradually subjected to Spanish colonial rule.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Conquest_of_the_Aztec_Triple_Alliance_(1519\xe2\x80\x931521)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_of_the_Aztec_Triple_Alliance_.281519.E2.80.931521.29">Conquest of the Aztec Triple Alliance (1519\xe2\x80\x931521)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish conquest of Mexico">Spanish conquest of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg/220px-Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg/330px-Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg/440px-Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg 2x" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="495" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hern\xc3\xa1n Cort\xc3\xa9s">Hern\xc3\xa1n Cort\xc3\xa9s</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Malinche" title="La Malinche">La Malinche</a> meet <a href="/wiki/Moctezuma_II" title="Moctezuma II">Moctezuma II</a>. The image is from the <i><a href="/wiki/Lienzo_de_Tlaxcala" class="mw-redirect" title="Lienzo de Tlaxcala">Lienzo de Tlaxcala</a></i>, created c. 1550 by the Tlaxcalans to remind the Spanish of their loyalty and the importance of <a href="/wiki/Tlaxcala_(Nahua_state)" title="Tlaxcala (Nahua state)">Tlaxcala</a> during the conquest.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Spanish first learned of Mexico during the <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Grijalva" title="Juan de Grijalva">Juan de Grijalva</a> expedition of 1518. The natives kept "repeating: <i>Colua, Colua</i>, and <i>Mexico, Mexico</i>, but we [explorers] did not know what <i>Colua</i> or <i>Mexico</i> meant", until encountering Montezuma\'s governor at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Boca_del_R%C3%ADo,_Veracruz" title="Boca del R\xc3\xado, Veracruz">Rio de las Banderas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Diaz_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diaz-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:33\xe2\x80\x9336</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire</a> began in February 1519 when <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hern\xc3\xa1n Cort\xc3\xa9s">Hern\xc3\xa1n Cort\xc3\xa9s</a> arrived at the port in <a href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" class="mw-redirect" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">Veracruz</a> with ca. 500 <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadores</a>. After taking control of that city, he moved on to the Aztec capital. In his search for gold and other riches, Cort\xc3\xa9s decided to invade and conquer the Aztec empire.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leutze,_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Leutze%2C_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg/220px-Leutze%2C_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Leutze%2C_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg/330px-Leutze%2C_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Leutze%2C_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg/440px-Leutze%2C_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1358" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leutze,_Emanuel_%E2%80%94_Storming_of_the_Teocalli_by_Cortez_and_His_Troops_%E2%80%94_1848.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nStorming of the <a href="/wiki/Teocalli" title="Teocalli">Teocalli</a> by Cortez and his troops. <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Leutze" title="Emanuel Leutze">Emanuel Leutze</a>. Painting, 1848</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>When the Spaniards arrived, the ruler of the Aztec empire was <a href="/wiki/Moctezuma_II" title="Moctezuma II">Moctezuma II</a>, who was later killed. His successor and brother <a href="/wiki/Cuitl%C3%A1huac" title="Cuitl\xc3\xa1huac">Cuitl\xc3\xa1huac</a> took control of the Aztec empire, but was among the first to fall from the first <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">epidemic</a> in the area a short time later.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Unintentionally introduced by Spanish conquerors, among whom <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> was endemic, the infectious disease ravaged Mesoamerica in the 1520s. It killed more than 3 million natives as they had no <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">immunity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Other sources, however, mentioned that the death toll of the Aztecs might have reached 15 million (out of a population of less than 30 million) although such a high number conflicts with the 350,000 Aztecs who ruled an empire of 5 million or 10 million.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Severely weakened, the Aztec empire was easily defeated by Cort\xc3\xa9s and his forces on his second return with the help of state of Tlaxcala whose population estimate was 300,000.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The native population declined 80\xe2\x80\x9390% by 1600 to 1\xe2\x80\x932.5 million. Any population estimate of pre-Columbian Mexico is bound to be a guess but 8\xe2\x80\x9312 million is often suggested for the area encompassed by the modern nation.</p>\n<p>Smallpox was a devastating disease: it generally killed Aztecs but not Spaniards, who as Europeans had already been exposed to it in their cities for centuries and therefore had developed acquired immunity.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The deaths caused by smallpox are believed to have triggered a rapid growth of Christianity in Mexico and the Americas. At first, the Aztecs believed the epidemic was a punishment from an angry god, but they later accepted their fate and no longer resisted the Spanish rule.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Many of the surviving Aztecs believed that smallpox could be credited to the superiority of the Christian god, which resulted in their acceptance of Catholicism and yielding to the Spanish rule throughout Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The territory became part of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> under the name of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> was systematically rebuilt by Cort\xc3\xa9s following the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Tenochtitlan" title="Fall of Tenochtitlan">Fall of Tenochtitlan</a> in 1521. Much of the identity, traditions and architecture of Mexico developed during the 300-year colonial period.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain_(1521\xe2\x80\x931821)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain_.281521.E2.80.931821.29">Viceroyalty of New Spain (1521\xe2\x80\x931821)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg/220px-El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg/330px-El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg/440px-El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="553" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_caballito_de_Tolsa_a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Equestrian_statue_of_Charles_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Equestrian statue of Charles IV">Equestrian statue of Charles IV</a>, Mexico City, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Tols%C3%A1" title="Manuel Tols\xc3\xa1">Manuel Tols\xc3\xa1</a>. The Spanish Monarch was the maximum authority in New Spain and ruled via a <a href="/wiki/List_of_viceroys_of_New_Spain" title="List of viceroys of New Spain">viceroy</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The capture of Tenochtitlan and refounding of Mexico City in 1521 was the beginning of a 300-year-long colonial era during which Mexico was known as <i>Nueva Espa\xc3\xb1a</i> (New Spain). The Kingdom of New Spain was created from the remnants of the Aztec hegemonic empire. Subsequent enlargements, such as the conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Tarascan_state" title="Tarascan state">Tarascan state</a>, resulted in the creation of the Viceroyalty of New Spain in 1535. The Viceroyalty at its greatest extent included the territories of modern Mexico, Central America as far south as Costa Rica, and the western United States. The Viceregal capital Mexico City also administrated the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish West Indies</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a>.</p>\n<p>The indigenous population stabilized around one to one and a half million individuals in the 17th century from the most commonly accepted five to ten million <a href="/wiki/Population_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">pre-contact population</a>. The population decline was primarily the result of communicable diseases, particularly <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, introduced during the <a href="/wiki/Columbian_Exchange" title="Columbian Exchange">Columbian Exchange</a>. During the three hundred years of the colonial era, Mexico received between 400,000 and 500,000 Europeans, between 200,000<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> and 250,000 Africans<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and between 40,000 and 120,000 Asians.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The 18th century saw a great increase in the percentage of mestizos.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Colonial <a href="/wiki/Law_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Law in Spain">law with Spanish roots</a> was introduced and attached to native customs creating a hierarchy between local jurisdiction (the <a href="/wiki/Cabildo_(council)" title="Cabildo (council)">Cabildos</a>) and the Spanish Crown. Whereby upper administrative offices were closed to native-born people, even those of pure Spanish blood (<a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">criollos</a>). Administration was based on the <a href="/wiki/Racial_separation" class="mw-redirect" title="Racial separation">racial separation</a> of the population among "Republics" of Spaniards, Amerindians and <i><a href="/wiki/Castas" class="mw-redirect" title="Castas">castas</a></i>, autonomous and directly dependent on the king himself.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_(1772).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg/170px-Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg/255px-Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg/340px-Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_%281772%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="968" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz_(1772).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nPortrait of Sor <a href="/wiki/Juana_Ines_de_la_Cruz" class="mw-redirect" title="Juana Ines de la Cruz">Juana Ines de la Cruz</a>, oil on canvas, 1772</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Indies">Council of Indies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mendicant_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Mendicant order">mendicant religious orders</a>, which arrived in Mesoamerica as early as 1524, labored to generate capital for the crown of Spain and convert the Amerindian populations to Catholicism. The 1531 <a href="/wiki/Marian_apparition" title="Marian apparition">Marian apparitions</a> to Saint <a href="/wiki/Juan_Diego" title="Juan Diego">Juan Diego</a> gave impetus to the evangelization of central Mexico. The <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Guadalupe" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin of Guadalupe">Virgin of Guadalupe</a> became a symbol of <i>criollo</i> patriotism<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and was used by the insurgents that followed Miguel Hidalgo during the War of Independence. Some <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">Crypto-Jewish</a> families emigrated to Mexico to escape the Spanish Inquisition.</p>\n<p>The rich deposits of silver, particularly in Zacatecas and Guanajuato, resulted in silver extraction dominating the economy of New Spain. <a href="/wiki/Royal_fifth" title="Royal fifth">Taxes on silver production</a> became a major source of income for Spain. Other important industries were the <a href="/wiki/Haciendas" class="mw-redirect" title="Haciendas">haciendas</a> (functioning under the <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomienda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Repartimiento" title="Repartimiento">repartimiento</a> systems) and mercantile activities in the main cities and ports. Wealth created during the colonial era spurred the development of <a href="/wiki/New_Spanish_Baroque" title="New Spanish Baroque">New Spanish Baroque</a>.</p>\n<p>As a result of its trade links with Asia, the rest of the Americas, Africa and Europe and the <a href="/wiki/Global_silver_trade_from_the_16th_to_18th_centuries" title="Global silver trade from the 16th to 18th centuries">profound effect of New World silver</a>, central Mexico was one of the first regions to be incorporated into a <a href="/wiki/Globalized" class="mw-redirect" title="Globalized">globalized</a> economy. Being at the crossroads of trade, people and cultures, Mexico City has been called the "first <a href="/wiki/World_city" class="mw-redirect" title="World city">world city</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Nao_de_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Nao de China">Nao de China</a></i> (Manila Galleons) operated for two and a half centuries and connected New Spain with Asia. Goods were taken from Veracruz to Atlantic ports in the Americas and Spain. Veracruz was also the main port of entry in mainland New Spain for European goods, immigrants, and African slaves. The <i><a href="/wiki/Camino_Real_de_Tierra_Adentro" title="Camino Real de Tierra Adentro">Camino Real de Tierra Adentro</a></i> connected Mexico City with the interior of New Spain.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg/220px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg/330px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg/440px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_a%C3%A9rea_de_Guanajuato.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Guanajuato_City" title="Guanajuato City">Guanajuato City</a> became the world\'s leading silver producer in the 18th century as a result of the <i><a href="/wiki/Mother_lode" title="Mother lode">veta madre</a></i>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Due to the importance of central New Spain, Mexico was the location of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_First_Print_Shop_in_the_Americas" title="House of the First Print Shop in the Americas">first printing shop</a> (1539), <a href="/wiki/Royal_and_Pontifical_University_of_Mexico" title="Royal and Pontifical University of Mexico">first university</a> (1551), <a href="/wiki/Alameda_Central" title="Alameda Central">first public park</a> (1592), and <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Palafoxiana" title="Biblioteca Palafoxiana">first public library</a> (1646) in the Americas, amongst other institutions. Important artists of the colonial period, include the writers <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ruiz_de_Alarc%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ruiz de Alarc\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ruiz de Alarc\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sor_Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz" class="mw-redirect" title="Sor Juana In\xc3\xa9s de la Cruz">Sor Juana In\xc3\xa9s de la Cruz</a>, painters <a href="/wiki/Crist%C3%B3bal_de_Villalpando" title="Crist\xc3\xb3bal de Villalpando">Crist\xc3\xb3bal de Villalpando</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cabrera_(painter)" title="Miguel Cabrera (painter)">Miguel Cabrera</a>, and architect <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Tols%C3%A1" title="Manuel Tols\xc3\xa1">Manuel Tols\xc3\xa1</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_San_Carlos" title="Academy of San Carlos">Academy of San Carlos</a> was the first major school and museum of art in the Americas. Scientist <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Manuel_del_R%C3%ADo_Fern%C3%A1ndez" class="mw-redirect" title="Andr\xc3\xa9s Manuel del R\xc3\xado Fern\xc3\xa1ndez">Andr\xc3\xa9s Manuel del R\xc3\xado Fern\xc3\xa1ndez</a> discovered the element <a href="/wiki/Vanadium" title="Vanadium">vanadium</a>.</p>\n<p>Spanish forces, sometimes accompanied by native allies, led expeditions to conquer territory or quell rebellions through the colonial era. Notable Amerindian revolts in sporadically populated northern New Spain include the <a href="/wiki/Chichimeca_War" title="Chichimeca War">Chichimeca War</a> (1576\xe2\x80\x931606), <a href="/wiki/Tepehu%C3%A1n_Revolt" title="Tepehu\xc3\xa1n Revolt">Tepehu\xc3\xa1n Revolt</a> (1616\xe2\x80\x931620) and the <a href="/wiki/Pueblo_Revolt" title="Pueblo Revolt">Pueblo Revolt</a> (1680). In order to protect Mexico from the attacks of English, French and Dutch <a href="/wiki/Pirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirates">pirates</a> and protect the Crown\'s monopoly of revenue, only two ports were open to foreign trade\xe2\x80\x94Veracruz on the Atlantic and Acapulco on the Pacific. Among the best-known pirate attacks are the 1663 <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Campeche_(1663)" title="Sack of Campeche (1663)">Sack of Campeche</a> and 1683 <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Veracruz" title="Attack on Veracruz">Attack on Veracruz</a>.</p>\n<p>Many Mexican cultural features including <a href="/wiki/Tequila" title="Tequila">tequila</a>, first distilled in the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Charreria" class="mw-redirect" title="Charreria">charreria</a> (17th), <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">mariachi</a> (18th) and <a href="/wiki/Mexican_cuisine" title="Mexican cuisine">Mexican cuisine</a>, a fusion <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">of American</a> and European (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine" title="Spanish cuisine">particularly Spanish</a>) cuisine, arose during the colonial era.</p>\n<h3><span id="War_of_Independence_(1810\xe2\x80\x931821)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_Independence_.281810.E2.80.931821.29">War of Independence (1810\xe2\x80\x931821)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG/220px-Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG/330px-Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG/440px-Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3056" data-file-height="2292" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abrazo_de_Acatempan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDepiction of the <i><a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abrazo_de_Acatempan" class="extiw" title="es:Abrazo de Acatempan">Abrazo de Acatempan</a></i> between <a href="/wiki/Agustin_de_Iturbide" class="mw-redirect" title="Agustin de Iturbide">Agustin de Iturbide</a>, left, and <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Guerrero" title="Vicente Guerrero">Vicente Guerrero</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On September 16, 1810, a "loyalist revolt" against the ruling Junta was declared by priest <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo_y_Costilla" title="Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla">Miguel Hidalgo y Costilla</a>, in the small town of <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Hidalgo" title="Dolores Hidalgo">Dolores</a>, Guanajuato.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The first insurgent group was formed by Hidalgo, the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Viceregal" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceregal">viceregal</a> army captain <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Allende" title="Ignacio Allende">Ignacio Allende</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militia</a> captain <a href="/wiki/Juan_Aldama" title="Juan Aldama">Juan Aldama</a> and "La Corregidora" <a href="/wiki/Josefa_Ortiz_de_Dom%C3%ADnguez" title="Josefa Ortiz de Dom\xc3\xadnguez">Josefa Ortiz de Dom\xc3\xadnguez</a>. Hidalgo and some of his soldiers were captured and <a href="/wiki/Executed_by_firing_squad" class="mw-redirect" title="Executed by firing squad">executed by firing squad</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chihuahua,_Chihuahua" class="mw-redirect" title="Chihuahua, Chihuahua">Chihuahua</a>, on July 31, 1811. Following his death, the leadership was assumed by priest <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Morelos" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Morelos">Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Morelos</a>, who occupied key southern cities.</p>\n<p>In 1813 the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Chilpancingo" title="Congress of Chilpancingo">Congress of Chilpancingo</a> was convened and, on November 6, signed the "<a href="/wiki/Solemn_Act_of_the_Declaration_of_Independence_of_Northern_America" title="Solemn Act of the Declaration of Independence of Northern America">Solemn Act of the Declaration of Independence of Northern America</a>". Morelos was captured and executed on December 22, 1815.</p>\n<p>In subsequent years, the insurgency was near collapse, but in 1820 <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">Viceroy</a> <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ruiz_de_Apodaca" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Ruiz de Apodaca">Juan Ruiz de Apodaca</a> sent an army under the <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">criollo</a> general <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_Iturbide" title="Agust\xc3\xadn de Iturbide">Agust\xc3\xadn de Iturbide</a> against the troops of <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Guerrero" title="Vicente Guerrero">Vicente Guerrero</a>. Instead, Iturbide approached Guerrero to join forces, and on August 24, 1821 representatives of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Crown">Spanish Crown</a> and Iturbide signed the "<a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Treaty of C\xc3\xb3rdoba">Treaty of C\xc3\xb3rdoba</a>" and the "<a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Mexican_Empire" title="Declaration of Independence of the Mexican Empire">Declaration of Independence of the Mexican Empire</a>", which recognized the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence of Mexico">independence of Mexico</a> under the terms of the "<a href="/wiki/Plan_of_Iguala" title="Plan of Iguala">Plan of Iguala</a>".</p>\n<p>Mexico\xe2\x80\x99s short recovery after the War of Independence was soon cut short again by the civil wars and institutional instability of the 1850s, which lasted until the government of Porfirio D\xc3\xadaz reestablished conditions that paved the way for economic growth. The conflicts that arose from the mid-1850s had a profound effect because they were widespread and made themselves perceptible in the vast rural areas of the countries, involved clashes between castes, different ethnic groups and haciendas, and entailed a deepening of the political and ideological divisions between republicans and monarchists.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="First_Empire_and_First_Republic_(1821\xe2\x80\x931846)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Empire_and_First_Republic_.281821.E2.80.931846.29">First Empire and First Republic (1821\xe2\x80\x931846)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">First Mexican Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Republic" title="First Mexican Republic">First Mexican Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Centralist_Republic_of_Mexico" title="Centralist Republic of Mexico">Centralist Republic of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png/220px-Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png/330px-Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png/440px-Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png 2x" data-file-width="1669" data-file-height="1518" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico%27s_Territorial_Evolution.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Mexico" title="Territorial evolution of Mexico">territorial evolution of Mexico</a> after independence, noting the secession of <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">Central America</a> (purple), Chiapas annexed from <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">Guatemala</a> (blue), losses to the US (red, white and orange) and the reannexation of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Yucatan" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Yucatan">Republic of Yucatan</a> (red)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Agust\xc3\xadn de Iturbide became constitutional emperor of the <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">First Mexican Empire</a> in 1822. A revolt against him in 1823 established the <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Republic" title="First Mexican Republic">United Mexican States</a>. In 1824, a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_1824" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of 1824">Republican Constitution</a> was drafted and <a href="/wiki/Guadalupe_Victoria" title="Guadalupe Victoria">Guadalupe Victoria</a> became the first president of the newly born country. Central America, including Chiapas, left the union. In 1829 president <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Guerrero" title="Vicente Guerrero">Guerrero</a> abolished <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavery_in_Mexico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Slavery in Mexico (page does not exist)">slavery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The first decades of the post-independence period were marked by <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Mexico" title="Economic history of Mexico">economic instability</a>, which led to the <a href="/wiki/Pastry_War" title="Pastry War">Pastry War</a> in 1836. There was constant strife between liberales, supporters of a <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal form of government</a>, and conservadores, who proposed a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">hierarchical form of government</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>During this period, the frontier borderlands to the north became quite isolated from the government in Mexico City, and its monopolistic economic policies caused suffering. With limited trade, the people had difficulty meeting tax payments and resented the central government\'s actions in collecting customs. Resentment built up from California to Texas. Both the mission system and the <i><a href="/wiki/Presidios" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidios">presidios</a></i> had collapsed after the Spanish withdrew from the colony, causing great disruption especially in Alta California and New Mexico. The people in the borderlands had to raise local militias to protect themselves from hostile Native Americans. These areas developed in different directions from the center of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-73">[73]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Wanting to stabilize and develop the frontier, Mexico encouraged immigration into present-day Texas, as they were unable to persuade people from central Mexico to move into those areas. They allowed for religious freedom for the new settlers, who were primarily Protestant English speakers from the United States. Within several years, the Anglos far outnumbered the <a href="/wiki/Tejano" title="Tejano">Tejano</a> in the area. Itinerant traders traveled through the area, working by free market principles. The Tejano grew more separate from the government and due to its neglect, many supported the idea of independence and joined movements to that end, collaborating with the English-speaking Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-73">[73]</a></sup></p>\n<p>General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio L\xc3\xb3pez de Santa Anna">Antonio L\xc3\xb3pez de Santa Anna</a>, a centralist and two-time dictator, approved the <a href="/wiki/Siete_Leyes" title="Siete Leyes">Siete Leyes</a> in 1836, a radical amendment that institutionalized the centralized form of government. When he suspended the 1824 Constitution, civil war spread across the country. Three new governments declared independence: the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Rio_Grande" title="Republic of the Rio Grande">Republic of the Rio Grande</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Republic of Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Republic of Yucat\xc3\xa1n</a>.</p>\n<h3><span id="Second_Republic_and_Second_Empire_(1846\xe2\x80\x931867)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Republic_and_Second_Empire_.281846.E2.80.931867.29">Second Republic and Second Empire (1846\xe2\x80\x931867)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Second_Mexican_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Mexican Republic">Second Mexican Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Mexican_Empire" title="Second Mexican Empire">Second Mexican Empire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BenitoJuarez.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BenitoJuarez.jpg/170px-BenitoJuarez.jpg" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BenitoJuarez.jpg/255px-BenitoJuarez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/BenitoJuarez.jpg 2x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="440" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BenitoJuarez.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Benito Ju\xc3\xa1rez">Benito Ju\xc3\xa1rez</a>, 26th President of Mexico</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The 1846 United States annexation of the Republic of Texas and subsequent American military incursion into territory that was part of Coahuila (also claimed by Texas) instigated the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican\xe2\x80\x93American War">Mexican\xe2\x80\x93American War</a>. The war was settled in 1848 via the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a>. Mexico was forced to give up more than one-third of its land to the U.S., including <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo M\xc3\xa9xico">Santa Fe de Nuevo M\xc3\xa9xico</a> and the territory claimed by Texas. A much smaller transfer of territory in what is today southern <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> and southwestern <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>\xe2\x80\x94known as the <a href="/wiki/Gadsden_Purchase" title="Gadsden Purchase">Gadsden Purchase</a>\xe2\x80\x94occurred in 1854.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Caste_War_of_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Caste War of Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Caste War of Yucat\xc3\xa1n</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maya_peoples" title="Maya peoples">Maya</a> uprising that began in 1847, was one of the most successful modern Native American revolts.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Maya rebels, or <a href="/wiki/Cruzob" class="mw-redirect" title="Cruzob">Cruzob</a>, maintained relatively independent enclaves in the peninsula until the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Dissatisfaction with Santa Anna\'s return to power led to the liberal "<a href="/wiki/Plan_of_Ayutla" title="Plan of Ayutla">Plan of Ayutla</a>", initiating an era known as <a href="/wiki/La_Reforma" title="La Reforma">La Reforma</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_1857" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of 1857">new Constitution drafted in 1857</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>, federalism as the <a href="/wiki/Form_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Form of government">form of government</a>, and several freedoms. As the conservadores refused to recognize it, the <a href="/wiki/Reform_War" title="Reform War">Reform War</a> began in 1858, during which both groups had their own governments. The war ended in 1861 with victory by the Liberals, led by president <a href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Benito Ju\xc3\xa1rez">Benito Ju\xc3\xa1rez</a>, who was an ethnic <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_peoples" title="Zapotec peoples">Zapotec</a>.</p>\n<p>In the 1860s <a href="/wiki/French_intervention_in_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="French intervention in Mexico">Mexico was occupied by France</a>, which established the <a href="/wiki/Second_Mexican_Empire" title="Second Mexican Empire">Second Mexican Empire</a> under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> Archduke <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_of_Mexico" title="Maximilian I of Mexico">Ferdinand Maximilian</a> of <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austria</a> with support from the Roman Catholic clergy and the <i>conservadores</i>. The latter switched sides and joined the <i>liberales</i>. Maximilian surrendered, was tried on June 14, 1867, and was executed a few days later on June 19 in Quer\xc3\xa9taro.</p>\n<h3><span id="Porfiriato_(1876\xe2\x80\x931911)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Porfiriato_.281876.E2.80.931911.29">Porfiriato (1876\xe2\x80\x931911)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Porfiriato" class="mw-redirect" title="Porfiriato">Porfiriato</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Porfirio_D%C3%ADaz" title="Porfirio D\xc3\xadaz">Porfirio D\xc3\xadaz</a>, a republican general during the French intervention, was elected the 29th president in 1876. The 1880 election was won by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Flores" title="Manuel Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Flores">Manuel Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Flores</a>. D\xc3\xadaz was reelected in 1884 and ruled until 1911. The period, known as the Porfiriato, was characterized by economic stability and growth, significant foreign investment and influence, investments in the arts and sciences and an expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Mexico" title="Rail transport in Mexico">railroad network</a> and telecommunications. The period was concurrent with the <a href="/wiki/Gilded_Age" title="Gilded Age">Gilded Age</a> in the US and <a href="/wiki/Belle_%C3%89poque" title="Belle \xc3\x89poque">Belle \xc3\x89poque</a> in France and was also marked by economic inequality and political repression.</p>\n<p>D\xc3\xadaz ruled with a group of confidants that became known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Cient%C3%ADfico" title="Cient\xc3\xadfico">cient\xc3\xadficos</a></i> ("scientists"). The most influential <i>cientifco</i> was Secretary of Finance <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Yves_Limantour" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Yves Limantour">Jos\xc3\xa9 Yves Limantour</a>. The Porfirian regime was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Positivism" title="Positivism">positivism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cientifico_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cientifico-78">[78]</a></sup> They rejected theology and <a href="/wiki/Idealism" title="Idealism">idealism</a> in favor of scientific methods being applied towards national development.<sup id="cite_ref-cientifico_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cientifico-78">[78]</a></sup> Various iconic buildings and monuments were initiated by D\xc3\xadaz, including the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Correos_de_Mexico" title="Palacio de Correos de Mexico">Palacio de Correos de Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monumento_a_la_Independencia" class="mw-redirect" title="Monumento a la Independencia">Monumento a la Independencia</a> and the Palacio Legislativo (which became the <a href="/wiki/Monumento_a_la_Revoluci%C3%B3n" title="Monumento a la Revoluci\xc3\xb3n">Monumento a la Revoluci\xc3\xb3n</a>).</p>\n<h3><span id="Mexican_Revolution_and_one-party_rule_(1910\xe2\x80\x932000)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexican_Revolution_and_one-party_rule_.281910.E2.80.932000.29">Mexican Revolution and one-party rule (1910\xe2\x80\x932000)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg/220px-Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage"
