title="Zacatecas">Zacatecas (ZAC)</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Zacatecas_City" title="Zacatecas City">Zacatecas</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mexico" title="Economy of Mexico">Economy of Mexico</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Mexico" title="Economic history of Mexico">Economic history of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1107" data-file-height="862" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA proportional representation of Mexico\'s exports. The country has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_complexity" title="List of countries by economic complexity">most complex economy</a> in Latin America.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexico has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">15th largest</a> nominal GDP and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">11th largest</a> by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. GDP annual average growth for the period of 1995\xe2\x80\x932002 was 5.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-Crandall_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crandall-87">[87]</a></sup> Mexico\'s Gross Domestic Product (GDP) in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) was estimated at US $2.2602 trillion in 2015, and $1.3673 trillion in nominal exchange rates.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-167">[167]</a></sup> Mexico\'s GDP in PPP per capita was US $18,714.05. The World Bank reported in 2009 that the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_National_Income" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross National Income">Gross National Income</a> in market exchange rates was the second highest in Latin America, after <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> at US $1,830.392&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-GNI_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GNI-168">[168]</a></sup> which lead to the highest <a href="/wiki/Gross_National_Income" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross National Income">income per capita</a> in the region at $14,400.<sup id="cite_ref-GNIPC_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GNIPC-169">[169]</a></sup> Mexico is now firmly established as an upper middle-income country. After the slowdown of 2001 the country has recovered and has grown 4.2, 3.0 and 4.8 percent in 2004, 2005 and 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> even though it is considered to be well below Mexico\'s potential growth.<sup id="cite_ref-Hufbauer_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hufbauer-171">[171]</a></sup> Furthermore, after the 2008\xe2\x80\x932009 recession, the economy grew an average of 3.32 percent per year from 2010 to 2014.</p>\n<p>From the late 1990s onwards, the majority of the population has been part of the growing middle class.<sup id="cite_ref-WB_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB-172">[172]</a></sup> But according to Mexico\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Council_for_the_Evaluation_of_Social_Development_Policy_(CONEVAL)" title="National Council for the Evaluation of Social Development Policy (CONEVAL)">National Council for the Evaluation of Social Development Policy</a> (CONEVAL) from 2006 to 2010 the portion of the population who were in poverty rose from 19% to 46% (52 million persons).<sup id="cite_ref-CONEVAL_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONEVAL-173">[173]</a></sup> However, rather than Mexico\xe2\x80\x99s economy crashing, international economists attribute the huge increase in the percentage of population living below the country\'s poverty line to the CONEVAL changing the standards used to define it, pointing out that the percentage of people living in poverty according Mexico\xe2\x80\x99s national poverty line is around 40 times higher than the one reported by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank\xe2\x80\x99s</a> international poverty line, with the difference between the two being the biggest in the world. It is pondered then if it wouldn\'t be better for countries in the situation of Mexico to adopt more internationalized standards to measure poverty so the numbers obtained could be used to make accurate international comparisons.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD\'s</a> own poverty line (defined as the percentage of a country\'s population who earns half or less of the national median income) 21.5% of the Mexico\'s population lives in situation of poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-OECDREFORMA_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECDREFORMA-175">[175]</a></sup> This is also reflected by the fact that infant mortality in Mexico is three times higher than the average among OECD nations, and the literacy levels are in the median range of OECD nations. Nevertheless, according to <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, by 2050 Mexico will have the 5th largest economy in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Among the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> countries, Mexico has the second highest degree of economic disparity between the extremely poor and extremely rich, after Chile&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 although it has been falling over the last decade, being only one of few countries in which this is the case.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The bottom ten percent in the income hierarchy disposes of 1.36% of the country\'s resources, whereas the upper ten percent dispose of almost 36%. OECD also notes that Mexico\'s budgeted expenses for poverty alleviation and social development is only about a third of the OECD average \xe2\x80\x93 both in absolute and relative numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-OECDREFORMA_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECDREFORMA-175">[175]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to a 2008 UN report the average income in a typical urbanized area of Mexico was $26,654, while the average income in rural areas just miles away was only $8,403.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Daily minimum wages are set annually being set at $80.04 <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">Mexican pesos</a> ($4.5 USD) in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The electronics industry of Mexico has grown enormously within the last decade. Mexico has the sixth largest electronics industry in the world after <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Mexico is the second largest exporter of electronics to the United States where it exported $71.4 billion worth of electronics in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-prnewswire.com_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire.com-180">[180]</a></sup> The Mexican electronics industry is dominated by the manufacture and OEM design of televisions, displays, computers, mobile phones, circuit boards, semiconductors, electronic appliances, communications equipment and LCD modules. The Mexican electronics industry grew 20% between 2010 and 2011, up from its constant growth rate of 17% between 2003 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-prnewswire.com_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire.com-180">[180]</a></sup> Currently electronics represent 30% of Mexico\'s exports.<sup id="cite_ref-prnewswire.com_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire.com-180">[180]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg/220px-Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg/330px-Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg/440px-Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciudad.de.Mexico.City.Distrito.Federal.DF.Paseo.Reforma.Skyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> is the most important financial and economic center in Mexico.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexico produces the most automobiles of any North American nation.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The industry produces technologically complex components and engages in some research and development activities.<sup id="cite_ref-Gereffi_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gereffi-182">[182]</a></sup> The "Big Three" (<a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford">Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a>) have been operating in Mexico since the 1930s, while <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> built their plants in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-Hufbauer_Auto_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hufbauer_Auto-183">[183]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Puebla,_Puebla" class="mw-redirect" title="Puebla, Puebla">Puebla</a> alone, 70 industrial part-makers cluster around Volkswagen.<sup id="cite_ref-Gereffi_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gereffi-182">[182]</a></sup> In the 2010s expansion of the sector was surging. In 2014 alone, more than $10 billion in investment was committed. In September 2016 Kia motors opened a $1 billion factory in <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Le%C3%B3n" title="Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n">Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> with Audi also opening an assembling plant in Puebla the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> currently have plants in constructuion.<sup id="cite_ref-KiaMexico_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KiaMexico-186">[186]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The domestic car industry is represented by <a href="/wiki/DINA_S.A." title="DINA S.A.">DINA S.A.</a>, which has built buses and trucks since 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> and the new <a href="/wiki/Mastretta" title="Mastretta">Mastretta</a> company that builds the high-performance <a href="/wiki/Mastretta_MXT" title="Mastretta MXT">Mastretta MXT</a> sports car.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> In 2006, trade with the United States and Canada accounted for almost 50% of Mexico\'s exports and 45% of its imports.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-13">[13]</a></sup> During the first three quarters of 2010, the United States had a $46.0 billion <a href="/wiki/Trade_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade deficit">trade deficit</a> with Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> In August 2010 Mexico surpassed France to become the 9th largest holder of US debt.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> The commercial and financial dependence on the US is a cause for concern.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The remittances from Mexican citizens working in the United States account for 0.2% of Mexico\'s GDP<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> which was equal to US$20 billion per year in 2004 and is the tenth largest source of foreign income after oil, industrial exports, manufactured goods, electronics, heavy industry, automobiles, construction, food, banking and financial services.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> According to Mexico\'s central bank, remittances in 2008 amounted to $25bn.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Major players in the broadcasting industry are <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a>, the largest Spanish media company in the Spanish-speaking world,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-195">[195]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/TV_Azteca" title="TV Azteca">TV Azteca</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Mexico" title="Telecommunications in Mexico">Telecommunications in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MORELOS_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/MORELOS_3.jpg/200px-MORELOS_3.jpg" width="200" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/MORELOS_3.jpg/300px-MORELOS_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/MORELOS_3.jpg/400px-MORELOS_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1385" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MORELOS_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMorelos 3, the latest addition to the <a href="/wiki/Morelos_Satellite_System" title="Morelos Satellite System">Morelos Satellite System</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The telecommunications industry is mostly dominated by <a href="/wiki/Telmex" title="Telmex">Telmex</a> (<i>Tel\xc3\xa9fonos de M\xc3\xa9xico</i>), privatized in 1990. By 2006, Telmex had expanded its operations to Colombia, Peru, Chile, Argentina, Brazil and Uruguay and the United States. Other players in the domestic industry are <a href="/wiki/Axtel" title="Axtel">Axtel</a> and Maxcom. Because of Mexican <a href="/wiki/Orography" title="Orography">orography</a>, providing a landline telephone service at remote mountainous areas is expensive, and the penetration of line-phones per capita is low compared to other Latin American countries, at 40 percent; however, 82% of Mexicans over the age of 14 own a mobile phone. Mobile telephony has the advantage of reaching all areas at a lower cost, and the total number of mobile lines is almost two times that of landlines, with an estimation of 63 million lines.<sup id="cite_ref-ciacom_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciacom-196">[196]</a></sup> The telecommunication industry is regulated by the government through <a href="/wiki/Cofetel" class="mw-redirect" title="Cofetel">Cofetel</a> (<i>Comisi\xc3\xb3n Federal de Telecomunicaciones</i>).</p>\n<p>The Mexican satellite system is domestic and operates 120 earth stations. There is also extensive microwave radio relay network and considerable use of fiber-optic and coaxial cable.<sup id="cite_ref-ciacom_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciacom-196">[196]</a></sup> Mexican satellites are operated by <i>Sat\xc3\xa9lites Mexicanos</i> (<a href="/wiki/Satmex" title="Satmex">Satmex</a>), a private company, leader in Latin America and servicing both North and South America.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> It offers broadcast, telephone and telecommunication services to 37 countries in the Americas, from Canada to <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>. Through business partnerships Satmex provides high-speed connectivity to ISPs and Digital Broadcast Services.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Satmex maintains its own satellite fleet with most of the fleet being designed and built in Mexico.</p>\n<p>The use of radio, television, and Internet in Mexico is prevalent.<sup id="cite_ref-encnations_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnations-199">[199]</a></sup> There are approximately 1,410 radio broadcast stations and 236 television stations (excluding repeaters).<sup id="cite_ref-ciacom_196-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciacom-196">[196]</a></sup> Major players in the broadcasting industry are <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a>\xe2\x80\x94the largest media company in the Spanish-speaking world<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-195">[195]</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94and <a href="/wiki/TV_Azteca" title="TV Azteca">TV Azteca</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Mexico" title="Electricity sector in Mexico">Electricity sector in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I,_Fase_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg/200px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg/300px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg/400px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1654" data-file-height="1104" /></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Central E\xc3\xb3lica Sureste I, Fase II in Oaxaca. The Isthmus of Tehuantepec is the region of Mexico with the highest capacity for wind energy. (see <i><a href="/wiki/Tehuantepecer" title="Tehuantepecer">Tehuantepecer</a></i>, a strong wind that affects the region)</div>\n</div>\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III,_Fase_1._(21526244958).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg/200px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg/300px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg/400px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5520" data-file-height="3680" /></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Central Geotermoel\xc3\xa9ctrica Azufres III in Michoac\xc3\xa1n. 100% of the electricity produced in Michoac\xc3\xa1n comes from renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-Geothermal_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geothermal-200">[200]</a></sup> 90% comes from <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric plants">hydroelectric plants</a>, and 10% from the Azufres <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">Geothermal</a> Field.<sup id="cite_ref-Geothermal_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geothermal-200">[200]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n<div style="clear:left"></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Energy production in Mexico is managed by state-owned companies: the <a href="/wiki/Comisi%C3%B3n_Federal_de_Electricidad" title="Comisi\xc3\xb3n Federal de Electricidad">Federal Commission of Electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pemex" title="Pemex">Pemex</a>.</p>\n<p>Pemex, the public company in charge of exploration, extraction, transportation and marketing of crude oil and natural gas, as well as the refining and distribution of petroleum products and petrochemicals, is one of the largest companies in the world by revenue, making US $86 billion in sales a year.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fortune_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> Mexico is the sixth-largest oil producer in the world, with 3.7 million barrels per day.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> In 1980 oil exports accounted for 61.6% of total exports; by 2000 it was only 7.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-Gereffi_182-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gereffi-182">[182]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The largest hydro plant in Mexico is the 2,400 MW <a href="/wiki/Chicoas%C3%A9n_Dam" title="Chicoas\xc3\xa9n Dam">Manuel Moreno Torres Dam</a> in Chicoas\xc3\xa9n, <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Grijalva_River" title="Grijalva River">Grijalva River</a>. This is the world\'s fourth most productive hydroelectric plant.<sup id="cite_ref-EIA_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-205">[205]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Mexico is the country with the world\'s third largest solar potential.<sup id="cite_ref-S.26G_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S.26G-206">[206]</a></sup> The country\'s gross solar potential is estimated at 5kWh/m2 daily, which corresponds to 50 times national electricity generation.<sup id="cite_ref-ER_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ER-207">[207]</a></sup> Currently, there is over 1 million square meters of <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar thermal">solar thermal</a> panels<sup id="cite_ref-SENER_2009b_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SENER_2009b-208">[208]</a></sup> installed in Mexico, while in 2005, there were 115,000 square meters of <a href="/wiki/Solar_PV" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar PV">solar PV</a> (photo-voltaic). It is expected that in 2012 there will be 1,8 million square meters of installed solar thermal panels.<sup id="cite_ref-SENER_2009b_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SENER_2009b-208">[208]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The project named <a href="/wiki/SEGH-CFE_1" title="SEGH-CFE 1">SEGH-CFE 1</a>, located in Puerto Libertad, Sonora, Northwest of Mexico, will have capacity of 46.8 MW from an array of 187,200 solar panels when complete in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Sonora_Energy_Group_Hermosillo_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sonora_Energy_Group_Hermosillo-209">[209]</a></sup> All of the electricity will be sold directly to the CFE and absorbed into the utility\'s transmission system for distribution throughout their existing network. At an installed capacity of 46.8 MWp, when complete in 2013, the project will be the first utility scale project of its kind in Mexico and the largest solar project of any kind in Latin America.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_Mexico" title="History of science and technology in Mexico">History of science and technology in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Autonomous_University_of_Mexico" title="National Autonomous University of Mexico">National Autonomous University of Mexico</a> was officially established in 1910,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> and the university become one of the most important institutes of higher learning in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-page285_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page285-211">[211]</a></sup> UNAM provides world class education in science, medicine, and engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Many scientific institutes and new institutes of higher learning, such as <a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="National Polytechnic Institute">National Polytechnic Institute</a> (founded in 1936),<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> were established during the first half of the 20th century. Most of the new research institutes were created within UNAM. Twelve institutes were integrated into UNAM from 1929 to 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-page18_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page18-214">[214]</a></sup> In 1959, the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Mexican Academy of Sciences">Mexican Academy of Sciences</a> was created to coordinate scientific efforts between academics.</p>\n<p>In 1995, the Mexican chemist <a href="/wiki/Mario_J._Molina" title="Mario J. Molina">Mario J. Molina</a> shared the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a> with <a href="/wiki/Paul_J._Crutzen" title="Paul J. Crutzen">Paul J. Crutzen</a> and <a href="/wiki/F._Sherwood_Rowland" title="F. Sherwood Rowland">F. Sherwood Rowland</a> for their work in atmospheric chemistry, particularly concerning the formation and decomposition of ozone.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Molina, an alumnus of UNAM, became the first Mexican citizen to win the Nobel Prize in science.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In recent years, the largest scientific project being developed in Mexico was the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Large_Millimeter_Telescope" title="Large Millimeter Telescope">Large Millimeter Telescope</a> (Gran Telescopio Milim\xc3\xa9trico, GMT), the world\'s largest and most sensitive single-aperture telescope in its frequency range.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> It was designed to observe regions of space obscured by stellar dust.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Mexico" title="Tourism in Mexico">Tourism in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios,_Cholula,_Puebla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios%2C_Cholula%2C_Puebla.jpg/250px-Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios%2C_Cholula%2C_Puebla.jpg" width="250" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios%2C_Cholula%2C_Puebla.jpg/375px-Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios%2C_Cholula%2C_Puebla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios%2C_Cholula%2C_Puebla.jpg/500px-Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios%2C_Cholula%2C_Puebla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="594" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios,_Cholula,_Puebla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_los_Remedios_(Mexico)" title="Iglesia de Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de los Remedios (Mexico)">Iglesia de Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de los Remedios</a> atop the <a href="/wiki/Great_Pyramid_of_Cholula" title="Great Pyramid of Cholula">Great Pyramid of Cholula</a> with <a href="/wiki/Popocat%C3%A9petl" title="Popocat\xc3\xa9petl">Popocat\xc3\xa9petl</a> visible in the background has become an iconic image of Mexico.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexico has traditionally been among the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">most visited countries in the world</a> according to the World Tourism Organization and it is the most visited country in the Americas, after the United States. The most notable attractions are the <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesoamerican">Mesoamerican</a> ruins, cultural festivals, colonial cities, nature reserves and the beach resorts. The nation\'s wide range of climates, from temperate to tropical, and unique culture \xe2\x80\x93 a fusion of the European and the Mesoamerican \xe2\x80\x93 make Mexico an attractive destination. The peak tourism seasons in the country are during December and the mid-Summer, with brief surges during the week before <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spring_break" title="Spring break">Spring break</a>, when many of the beach resort sites become popular destinations for college students from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.</p>\n<p>As of 2016, Mexico was the 8th most visited country in the world and had the 14th highest income from tourism in the world which is also the highest in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> The vast majority of tourists come to Mexico from the United States and Canada followed by Europe and Asia. A smaller number also come from other Latin American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> In the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Travel_and_Tourism_Competitiveness_Report" title="Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report">Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report</a>, Mexico was ranked 22nd in the world, which was 3rd in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg/220px-Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg/330px-Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg/440px-Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1600" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cozumel_Punta_Sur_View-27527.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe Caribbean state of <a href="/wiki/Quintana_Roo" title="Quintana Roo">Quintana Roo</a> is particularly known for beach tourism. Major destinations include Canc\xc3\xban, <a href="/wiki/Cozumel" title="Cozumel">Cozumel</a> and the Riviera Maya.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The coastlines of Mexico harbor many stretches of beaches that are frequented by sun bathers and other visitors. <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico#Article_27" title="Constitution of Mexico">According to national law</a>, the entirety of the coastlines are under federal ownership, that is, all beaches in the country are <a href="/wiki/Public_property" title="Public property">public</a>. On the Yucat\xc3\xa1n peninsula, one of the most popular beach destinations is the resort town of <a href="/wiki/Canc%C3%BAn" title="Canc\xc3\xban">Canc\xc3\xban</a>, especially among <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">students</a> during <a href="/wiki/Spring_break" title="Spring break">spring break</a>. Just offshore is the beach island of <a href="/wiki/Isla_Mujeres" title="Isla Mujeres">Isla Mujeres</a>, and to the east is the <a href="/wiki/Isla_Holbox" title="Isla Holbox">Isla Holbox</a>. To the south of Cancun is the coastal strip called <a href="/wiki/Riviera_Maya" title="Riviera Maya">Riviera Maya</a> which includes the beach town of <a href="/wiki/Playa_del_Carmen" title="Playa del Carmen">Playa del Carmen</a> and the ecological parks of <a href="/wiki/Xcaret" title="Xcaret">Xcaret</a> and Xel-H\xc3\xa1. A day trip to the south of Canc\xc3\xban is the historic port of <a href="/wiki/Tulum" title="Tulum">Tulum</a>. In addition to its beaches, the town of Tulum is notable for its cliff-side <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayan</a> ruins.</p>\n<p>On the <a href="/wiki/Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific">Pacific</a> coast is the notable tourist destination of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>. Once the destination for the rich and famous, the beaches have become crowded and the shores are now home to many multi-story hotels and vendors. Acapulco is home to renowned cliff divers: trained divers who leap from the side of a vertical cliff into the surf below.</p>\n<p>At the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a> is the resort town of <a href="/wiki/Cabo_San_Lucas" title="Cabo San Lucas">Cabo San Lucas</a>, a town noted for its beaches and <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">marlin</a> <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Further north along the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Cort%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea of Cort\xc3\xa9s">Sea of Cort\xc3\xa9s</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_Concepci%C3%B3n,_Baja_California_Sur" title="Bah\xc3\xada Concepci\xc3\xb3n, Baja California Sur">Bah\xc3\xada de La Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a>, another beach town known for its sports fishing. Closer to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> border is the weekend draw of <a href="/wiki/San_Felipe,_Baja_California" title="San Felipe, Baja California">San Felipe, Baja California</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Mexico" title="Transportation in Mexico">Transportation in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg/220px-Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg/330px-Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg/440px-Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Baluarte_Bridge" title="Baluarte Bridge">Baluarte Bridge</a> is the highest cable-stayed bridge in the world, the fifth-highest bridge overall and the highest bridge in the Americas.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The roadway network in Mexico is extensive and all areas in the country are covered by it.<sup id="cite_ref-nations_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nations-222">[222]</a></sup> The roadway network in Mexico has an extent of 366,095&#160;km (227,481&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-sctroad_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sctroad-223">[223]</a></sup> of which 116,802&#160;km (72,577&#160;mi) are paved,<sup id="cite_ref-sctroad-2_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sctroad-2-224">[224]</a></sup> making it the largest paved-roadway network in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Of these, 10,474&#160;km (6,508&#160;mi) are multi-lane <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">expressways</a>: 9,544&#160;km (5,930&#160;mi) are four-lane highways and the rest have 6 or more lanes.<sup id="cite_ref-sctroad-2_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sctroad-2-224">[224]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Mexico was one of the first Latin American countries to promote railway development,<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-117">[117]</a></sup> and the network covers 30,952&#160;km (19,233&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-encnations_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnations-199">[199]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_Communications_and_Transportation_(Mexico)" title="Secretariat of Communications and Transportation (Mexico)">Secretary of Communications and Transport</a> of Mexico proposed a high-speed rail link that will transport its passengers from <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-azcentral.com_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azcentral.com-226">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> The train, which will travel at 300 kilometres per hour (190 miles per hour),<sup id="cite_ref-systra.com_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-systra.com-228">[228]</a></sup> will allow passengers to travel from Mexico City to Guadalajara in just 2&#160;hours.<sup id="cite_ref-systra.com_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-systra.com-228">[228]</a></sup> The whole project was projected to cost 240&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/MXN" class="mw-redirect" title="MXN">pesos</a>, or about 25&#160;billion US$<sup id="cite_ref-azcentral.com_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azcentral.com-226">[226]</a></sup> and is being paid for jointly by the Mexican government and the local private sector including the wealthiest man in the world, Mexico\'s billionaire business tycoon <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Slim" title="Carlos Slim">Carlos Slim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> The government of the state of <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yucat\xc3\xa1n (state)">Yucat\xc3\xa1n</a> is also funding the construction of a high speed line connecting the cities of <a href="/wiki/Cozumel" title="Cozumel">Cozumel</a> to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="M\xc3\xa9rida, Yucat\xc3\xa1n">M\xc3\xa9rida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chichen_Itza" title="Chichen Itza">Chichen Itza</a> and Canc\xc3\xban.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Mexico has 233 airports with paved runways; of these, 35 carry 97% of the passenger traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-encnations_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnations-199">[199]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport" title="Mexico City International Airport">Mexico City International Airport</a> remains the largest in Latin America and the 44th largest in the world<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> transporting 21 million passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Mexico" title="Water supply and sanitation in Mexico">Water supply and sanitation in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Among the achievements is a significant increase in access to piped water supply in urban areas (88% to 93%) as well as in rural areas (50% to 74%) between 1990 and 2010. Additionally, a strong nationwide increase in access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">improved sanitation</a> (64% to 85%) was observed in the same period. Other achievements include the existence of a functioning national system to finance water and sanitation infrastructure with a National Water Commission as its apex institution; and the existence of a few well-performing utilities such as Aguas y Drenaje de Monterrey.</p>\n<p>The challenges include water scarcity in the northern and central parts of the country; inadequate water service quality (drinking water quality; 11% of Mexicans receiving water only intermittently as of 2014);<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> poor technical and commercial efficiency of most utilities (with an average level of <a href="/wiki/Non-revenue_water" title="Non-revenue water">non-revenue water</a> of 43.2% in 2010);<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> an insufficient share of wastewater receiving treatment (36% in 2006); and still inadequate access in rural areas. In addition to on-going investments to expand access, the government has embarked on a large investment program to improve wastewater treatment.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mexico" title="Demographics of Mexico">Demographics of Mexico</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">\n<tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical population</th>\n</tr>\n<tr style="font-size:95%">\n<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th>\n<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th>\n<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">\xc2\xb1%</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1910</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">15,160,369</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x80\x94&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1921</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">14,334,780</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x925.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1970</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">48,225,238</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+236.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2015</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">121,005,816</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+150.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: <a href="/wiki/INEGI" class="mw-redirect" title="INEGI">INEGI</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>According to estimations made by Mexico\'s <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Estad%C3%ADstica_y_Geograf%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Instituto Nacional de Estad\xc3\xadstica y Geograf\xc3\xada">National Geography and Statistics Institute</a>, as of 2017 Mexico has 123.5 million inhabitants<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> making it the most populous Spanish-speaking country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Spanishhistory_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spanishhistory-236">[236]</a></sup> Between 2005 and 2010, the Mexican population grew at an average of 1.70% per year, up from 1.16% per year between 2000 and 2005.</p>\n<p>Even though Mexico is a very ethnically diverse country, research about ethnicity has largely been a forgotten field, in consequence of the post-revolutionary efforts of Mexico\'s government to unify all Mexicans under a single ethnic identity (that of the "Mestizo"). As a result, since 1930 the only ethnic classification that has been included in Mexican censuses has been that of "Indigenous peoples".<sup id="cite_ref-EL_MESTIZAJE_Y_LAS_CULTURAS_REGIONALES_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EL_MESTIZAJE_Y_LAS_CULTURAS_REGIONALES-237">[237]</a></sup> Even then, across the years the government has used different criteria to count Indigenous peoples, with each of them returning considerably different numbers. It is not until very recently that the Mexican government begun conducting surveys that considered the <a href="/wiki/Afro-Mexican" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Mexican">Afro-Mexican</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexicans_of_European_descent" title="Mexicans of European descent">Euro-Mexican</a> population that lives in the country.</p>\n<p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the foreign-born population was 1,007,063.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> The majority of these individuals were born in the United States and Mexico is home to the <a href="/wiki/American_immigration_to_Mexico" title="American immigration to Mexico">largest number of U.S. citizens abroad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S.-239">[239]</a></sup> After Americans the largest immigrant groups are <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_immigration_to_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Guatemalan immigration to Mexico">Guatemalans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spaniards_in_Mexico" title="Spaniards in Mexico">Spaniards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Mexicans" title="Colombian Mexicans">Colombians</a>. Besides the Spanish, large immigrant-descended groups are the <a href="/wiki/French_immigration_to_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="French immigration to Mexico">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Mexicans" title="German Mexicans">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Mexicans" title="Lebanese Mexicans">Lebanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Mexicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Mexicans">Chinese</a>. Mexico is the largest source of immigration to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> Some 11.6 million residents of the United States have Mexican citizenship as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity_and_race">Ethnicity and race</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px">\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:131px;max-width:131px">\n<div class="thumbimage" style="height:164px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:De_espa%C3%B1ol_e_india,_mestiza.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/De_espa%C3%B1ol_e_india%2C_mestiza.jpg/129px-De_espa%C3%B1ol_e_india%2C_mestiza.jpg" width="129" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/De_espa%C3%B1ol_e_india%2C_mestiza.jpg/194px-De_espa%C3%B1ol_e_india%2C_mestiza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/De_espa%C3%B1ol_e_india%2C_mestiza.jpg/258px-De_espa%C3%B1ol_e_india%2C_mestiza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="777" data-file-height="995" /></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>De espa\xc3\xb1ol e india, mestiza</i>, 1763,<br />\n<a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cabrera_(painter)" title="Miguel Cabrera (painter)">Miguel Cabrera</a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:129px;max-width:129px">\n<div class="thumbimage" style="height:164px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:De_espa%C3%B1ol_y_negra,_mulata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/De_espa%C3%B1ol_y_negra%2C_mulata.jpg/127px-De_espa%C3%B1ol_y_negra%2C_mulata.jpg" width="127" height="164" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/De_espa%C3%B1ol_y_negra%2C_mulata.jpg/191px-De_espa%C3%B1ol_y_negra%2C_mulata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/De_espa%C3%B1ol_y_negra%2C_mulata.jpg/254px-De_espa%C3%B1ol_y_negra%2C_mulata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="825" data-file-height="1067" /></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>De espa\xc3\xb1ol y negra, mulata</i>, 1763,<br />\nMiguel Cabrera</div>\n</div>\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px">\n<div class="thumbimage" style="height:164px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:De_negro_e_india,_china_cambuja.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/De_negro_e_india%2C_china_cambuja.jpg/124px-De_negro_e_india%2C_china_cambuja.jpg" width="124" height="164" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/De_negro_e_india%2C_china_cambuja.jpg/186px-De_negro_e_india%2C_china_cambuja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/De_negro_e_india%2C_china_cambuja.jpg/248px-De_negro_e_india%2C_china_cambuja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="736" data-file-height="975" /></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>De negro e india, zamba</i>, 1763,<br />\nMiguel Cabrera</div>\n</div>\n<div style="clear:left"></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Depictions of the three main <i><a href="/wiki/Castas" class="mw-redirect" title="Castas">castas</a></i> resulting from miscegenation of Europeans, Africans and indigenous Americans. Produced during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_Enlightenment" title="Spanish American Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>, the <i>pinturas de castas</i> attempted to "rationally categorize" the racial diversity of Mexico, but some sets were also manifestations of early national self-pride. Wealth and order depicted through clothing, mercantile goods and religious symbols, challenged preconceived notions of New Spain in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexico is ethnically diverse; with people of several ethnicities being united under a single national identity.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated115_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated115-243">[243]</a></sup> The core part of Mexican national identity is formed on the basis of a synthesis of cultures, primarily European culture and indigenous cultures, in a process known as <a href="/wiki/Mestizaje" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizaje">mestizaje</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated115_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated115-243">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-census_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-244">[244]</a></sup> Mexican politicians and reformers such as <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vasconcelos" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos">Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos</a> (promoter of the <i><a href="/wiki/La_Raza_C%C3%B3smica" title="La Raza C\xc3\xb3smica">cosmic race</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Gamio" title="Manuel Gamio">Manuel Gamio</a> (promoter of <i><a href="/wiki/Indigenismo" title="Indigenismo">indigenismo</a></i>) were instrumental in building a Mexican national identity on the concept of mestizaje.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight.2C_Alan_1990._pp._78_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight.2C_Alan_1990._pp._78-245">[245]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The large majority of Mexicans have historically been classified as "<a href="/wiki/Mestizos_in_Mexico" title="Mestizos in Mexico">Mestizos</a>". In modern Mexican usage, the term <i>mestizo</i> is primarily a cultural identity rather than the racial identity it was during the colonial era, resulting in individuals with varying phenotypes being classified under the same identity, regardless of wheter they are of mixed ancestry or not.<sup id="cite_ref-redalyc_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-redalyc-246">[246]</a></sup> Since the term carries a variety of different socio-cultural, economic, racial and biological meanings, it was deemed too imprecise to be used for ethnic classification, thus it was abandoned by the government and is not in wide use in Mexican society,<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_117-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> although it\'s often used in literature about Mexican social identities and on intellectual circles. In the Yucat\xc3\xa1n peninsula the word Mestizo has historically had a different meaning, being used to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Yucatec_Maya_language" title="Yucatec Maya language">Maya</a>-speaking populations living in traditional communities, because during the <a href="/wiki/Caste_War_of_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Caste War of Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Caste War</a> of the late 19th century those Maya who did not join the rebellion were classified as mestizos.<sup id="cite_ref-Bartolom.C3.A9_1996:2_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartolom.C3.A9_1996:2-248">[248]</a></sup> In Chiapas the word "Ladino" is used instead of mestizo.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica">Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica</a> racially Mestizo Mexicans make up 50% to 67% of the country\'s population.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica-250">[250]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The total percentage of Mexico\'s population who is <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Mexico" title="Indigenous peoples of Mexico">indigenous</a> varies considerably depending of the criteria used by the government on its censuses: it is 5.4% if the hability to speak an indigenous language is used as the criteria to define a person as indigenous,<sup id="cite_ref-inegiindigenous_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inegiindigenous-251">[251]</a></sup> if racial self-identification is used it\'s 14.9%<sup id="cite_ref-CDI1_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDI1-252">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> and if people who considers themselves part indigenous are also included it amounts to 21.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-beta.inegi.org.mx_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beta.inegi.org.mx-254">[254]</a></sup> Nonetheless all the censuses conclude that the majority of Mexico\'s indigenous population is concentrated in the southern and south-eastern Mexican states, primarily in rural areas. Some indigenous communities have a degree of autonomy under the legislation of "usos y costumbres", which allows them to regulate some internal issues under <a href="/wiki/Customary_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Customary law">customary law</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/National_Commission_for_the_Development_of_Indigenous_Peoples" title="National Commission for the Development of Indigenous Peoples">National Commission for the Development of Indigenous Peoples</a>, the states with the greatest proportion of indigenous residents are:<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> Yucat\xc3\xa1n at 59%, Quintana Roo 39% and Campeche 27%, chiefly <a href="/wiki/Maya_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya people">Maya</a>; Oaxaca with 48% of the population, the most numerous groups being the <a href="/wiki/Mixtec" title="Mixtec">Mixtec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Zapotec people">Zapotec peoples</a>; Chiapas at 28%, the majority being <a href="/wiki/Tzeltal" class="mw-redirect" title="Tzeltal">Tzeltal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tzotzil_people" title="Tzotzil people">Tzotzil</a> Maya; Hidalgo 24%, the majority being <a href="/wiki/Otomi_people" title="Otomi people">Otomi</a>; Puebla 19%, and Guerrero 17%, mostly <a href="/wiki/Nahua_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahua people">Nahua peoples</a> and the states of San Luis Potos\xc3\xad and Veracruz both home to a population that is 15% indigenous, mostly from the <a href="/wiki/Totonac" class="mw-redirect" title="Totonac">Totonac</a>, Nahua and <a href="/wiki/Huastec_people" title="Huastec people">Teenek (Huastec)</a> groups.<sup id="cite_ref-inegi.org.mx_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inegi.org.mx-256">[256]</a></sup> The absolute numbers of the indigenous population growing, but at a slower rate than the rest of the population so that the percentage of indigenous peoples in regards to total population is nonetheless falling.<sup id="cite_ref-CDI_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDI-257">[257]</a></sup> All of the indices of social development for the indigenous population are considerably lower than the national average. In all states indigenous people have higher <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a>, in some states almost double of the non-indigenous populations. Literacy rates are also much lower, with 27% of indigenous children between 6 and 14 being illiterate compared to a national average of 12%. The indigenous population participate in the workforce longer than the national average, starting earlier and continuing longer. However, 55% of the indigenous population receive less than a minimum salary, compared to 20% for the national average. Many practice subsistence agriculture and receive no salaries. Indigenous people also have less access to health care and a lower quality of housing.<sup id="cite_ref-inegi.org.mx_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inegi.org.mx-256">[256]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Similarly to Mestizo and Indigenous peoples, estimations for the percentage of <a href="/wiki/Mexicans_of_European_descent" title="Mexicans of European descent">European-descended Mexicans</a> within the Mexican population vary considerably: their numbers range from around 10%\xe2\x80\x9320% according to the Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica-250">[250]</a></sup> to as high as 47%<sup id="cite_ref-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017-258">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conapred.org.mx_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conapred.org.mx-259">[259]</a></sup> according to a nationwide survey conducted by Mexico\'s government, made with the intent of having a precise outlook of the social and economic inequalities that exist between light skinned European looking Mexicans and Indigenous or African looking Mexicans,<sup id="cite_ref-DISC-RACIAL_2011_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC-RACIAL_2011-260">[260]</a></sup> is the first time the Mexican government has conducted an official population study that referenced Mexico\'s white population in nearly a century.<br />\nWhile during the colonial era, most of the European migration into Mexico was <a href="/wiki/Spaniards_in_Mexico" title="Spaniards in Mexico">Spanish</a>, in the 19th and 20th centuries a substantial number of non-Spanish Europeans immigrated to the country. According to 20th and 21st century academics, large scale intermixing between European immigrants and native Indigenous peoples would produce a Mestizo group which would become the overwhelming majority of Mexico\'s population by the time of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican revolution">Mexican revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fnavarrete_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fnavarrete-261">[261]</a></sup> However, according to church registers from the colonial times, the majority of European men married with European women. Said registers also put in question other narratives held by contemporary academics, such as European migrants who arrived to Mexico being almost exclusively men.<sup id="cite_ref-scielo.org.mx2_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scielo.org.mx2-262">[262]</a></sup> Nowadays Mexico\xe2\x80\x99s northern and western regions have the highest European populations, with the majority of the people not having native admixture or being of predominantly European ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-UnitedStatesandMexico_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnitedStatesandMexico-263">[263]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Afro-Mexican" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Mexican">Afro-Mexican</a> population (1,381,853 individuals as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-Encuesta_Intercensal_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encuesta_Intercensal-264">[264]</a></sup> is an ethnic group made up of descendants of Colonial-era slaves and recent immigrants of sub-Saharan African descent. Mexico had an active slave trade during the colonial period and some 200,000 Africans were taken there, primarily in the 17th century. The creation of a national Mexican identity, especially after the Mexican Revolution, emphasized Mexico\'s indigenous and European past; it passively eliminated the African ancestors and contributions. Most of the African-descended population was absorbed into the surrounding Mestizo (mixed European/indigenous) and indigenous populations through unions among the groups. Evidence of this long history of intermarriage with Mestizo and indigenous Mexicans is also expressed in the fact that in the 2015 inter-census, 64.9% (896,829) of Afro-Mexicans also identified as indigenous. It was also reported that 9.3% of Afro-Mexicans speak an indigenous language.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> The states with the highest self-report of Afro-Mexicans were Guerrero (6.5% of the population), Oaxaca (4.95%) and Veracruz (3.28%).<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> Afro-Mexican culture is strongest in the communities of the <a href="/wiki/Costa_Chica_of_Oaxaca" class="mw-redirect" title="Costa Chica of Oaxaca">Costa Chica of Oaxaca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Costa_Chica_of_Guerrero" title="Costa Chica of Guerrero">Costa Chica of Guerrero</a>.</p>\n<p>During the early 20th century, a substantial number of <a href="/wiki/Arab_Mexicans" title="Arab Mexicans">Arabs</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Arab_Christians" title="Arab Christians">Christians</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> began arriving from the crumbling <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. The largest group were the Lebanese and an estimated 400,000 Mexicans have some <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Mexicans" title="Lebanese Mexicans">Lebanese ancestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> Smaller ethnic groups in Mexico include <a href="/wiki/Asian_Mexicans" title="Asian Mexicans">South and East Asians</a>, present since the colonial era. During the colonial era Asians were termed <i>Chino</i> (regardless of ethnicity), and arrived as merchants, artisans and slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Seijas_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seijas-269">[269]</a></sup> The largest group were Filipinos and some 200,000 Mexicans can trace <a href="/wiki/Filipino_immigration_to_Mexico" title="Filipino immigration to Mexico">Filipino ancestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> Modern Asian immigration began in the late 19th century and at one point in the early 20th century, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_immigration_to_Mexico" title="Chinese immigration to Mexico">Chinese</a> were the second largest immigrant group.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_censuses">Official censuses</span></h4>\n<p>The first census in Mexico that included an ethnic classification was the 1793 census. Also known as the Revillagigedo census, it was Mexico\'s (then known as <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">New Spain</a>) first national population census. Most of its original datasets have reportedly been lost, thus most of what is known about it nowadays comes from essays and field investigations made by academics who had access to the census data and used it as reference for their works such as Prussian geographer <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a>. While every author gives different estimations for each racial group in the country they don\'t seem to vary much, with Europeans ranging from 18% to 22% of New Spain\'s population, Mestizos ranging from 21% to 25%, Indians ranging from 51% to 61% and Africans being between 6,000 and 10,000, The estimations given for the total population range from 3,799,561 to 6,122,354. It is concluded then, that across nearly three centuries of colonization, the population growth trends of whites and mestizos were even, while the total percentage of the indigenous population decreased at a rate of 13%\xe2\x80\x9317% per century. The authors assert that rather than whites and mestizos having higher birthrates, the reason for the indigenous population\'s numbers decreasing lies on them suffering of higher mortality rates, due living in remote locations rather than on cities and towns founded by the Spanish colonists or being at war with them.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> Anthropologist <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonzalo_Aguirre_Beltr%C3%A1n" class="extiw" title="es:Gonzalo Aguirre Beltr\xc3\xa1n">Gonzalo Aguirre Beltr\xc3\xa1n</a> goes beyond said numbers and splits the Mestizo group into "Euromestizos", "Indomestizos" and "Afromestizos" calculating their numbers on more than one million, 700,000 and 600,000 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Aguirre_Beltr.C3.A1n_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aguirre_Beltr.C3.A1n-273">[273]</a></sup> Independent-era Mexico eliminated the legal basis of the <a href="/wiki/Castas" class="mw-redirect" title="Castas">Colonial caste system</a> which led to exclude racial classification in the censuses to come.</p>\n<p>According to Mexico\'s second census ever which considered race, made right after the Mexican revolution on 1921,<sup id="cite_ref-somosprimos.com_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somosprimos.com-274">[274]</a></sup> 59% of Mexico\'s population was Mestizo, 29% was Indigenous and only 9% was European, with Mestizos being the most numerous ethno-racial group in almost all the states.<sup id="cite_ref-somosprimos.com_274-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somosprimos.com-274">[274]</a></sup> For a long time this census\' results have been taken as fact, with extraofficial international publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica">Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica</a> using them as a reference to estimate Mexico\'s racial composition up to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-275">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica_250-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica-250">[250]</a></sup> However, in recent time Mexican academics have subjected the census\' results to scrutiny, claiming that such a drastic alteration on demographic trends in regards to the 1793 census is not possible and cite, among other statistics the relatively low frequency of marriages between people of different continental ancestries in colonial and early independent Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> Said authors claim that the Mexican society went through a "more cultural than biological mestizaje process" sponsored by the state on its efforts to unify the Mexican population which resulted on the inflation of the percentage of the Mestizo Mexican group at the expense of the identity of the other races that exist in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In recent times the Mexican government has decided to conduct ethnic surveys and censuses again, and has also widen the criteria to classify the ethnicies who were already considered, an example being the Indigenous Mexican classification, which was previously reserved to people who lived in indigenous communities and/or spoke an indigenous language. According to these recent surveys Indigenous peoples amount to 21.5% of Mexico\'s population (including people who declared to be partially indigenous),<sup id="cite_ref-beta.inegi.org.mx_254-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beta.inegi.org.mx-254">[254]</a></sup> Afro-Mexicans are 1.2% of Mexico\'s population (including people who declared to be partially African)<sup id="cite_ref-beta.inegi.org.mx_254-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beta.inegi.org.mx-254">[254]</a></sup> and European Mexicans amount to 47% of Mexico\'s population (based on appearance rather than on self-declared of ancestry).<sup id="cite_ref-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017_258-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017-258">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conapred.org.mx_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conapred.org.mx-259">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DISC-RACIAL_2011_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC-RACIAL_2011-260">[260]</a></sup> Less numerous groups in Mexico such as Asians and Middle Easterners are also accounted for, albeit their numbers do not vary significantly from previous estimations. Out of all the ethnic groups that have recently been surveyed, that of Mestizos is notably absent, which may be consequence of the ethnic label\'s fluid and subjective definition, which complicates a precise calculation as well the tendency that Mexicans have to identify people with "static" ethnic labels rather than "fluid" ones.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Mexico" title="Languages of Mexico">Languages of Mexico</a></div>\n<p>The country has the largest Spanish-speaking population in the world with almost a third of all Spanish native speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-Spanishhistory_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spanishhistory-236">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Almost all of the Mexican population speaks Spanish, 99.3% according to the latest census;<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> nonetheless around 5.4% still speaks an indigenous language besides Spanish. The indigenous languages with the most speakers are <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a>, spoken by approximately 1.45 million people,<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yukatek_Maya" class="mw-redirect" title="Yukatek Maya">Yukatek Maya</a> spoken by some 750,000 people and the <a href="/wiki/Mixtec_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixtec languages">Mixtec</a><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_languages" title="Zapotec languages">Zapotec languages</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> each spoken by more than 400,000 people.</p>\n<p>The National Institute of Indigenous Languages <a href="/wiki/INALI" class="mw-redirect" title="INALI">INALI</a> recognizes 68 linguistic groups and some 364 different specific varieties of indigenous languages.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Since the promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Ley_General_de_Derechos_Ling%C3%BC%C3%ADsticos_de_los_Pueblos_Ind%C3%ADgenas" title="Ley General de Derechos Ling\xc3\xbc\xc3\xadsticos de los Pueblos Ind\xc3\xadgenas">Law of Indigenous Linguistic Rights</a> in 2003, these languages have had status as national languages, with equal validity with Spanish in all the areas and contexts in which they are spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In addition to the indigenous languages, other minority languages are spoken by immigrant populations, such as the 80,000 German-speaking <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Mexico" title="Mennonites in Mexico">Mennonites in Mexico</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup> and 5,000 speakers of the <a href="/wiki/Chipilo_Venetian_dialect" title="Chipilo Venetian dialect">Chipilo dialect</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian language</a> spoken in <a href="/wiki/Chipilo" title="Chipilo">Chipilo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> is the most commonly spoken foreign language in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_areas">Urban areas</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas_of_Mexico" title="Metropolitan areas of Mexico">Metropolitan areas of Mexico</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Mexico" title="List of cities in Mexico">List of cities in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Here are the 20 largest urban areas in Mexico.</p>\n<table href="/wiki/Guadalajara_Metropolitan_Area" title="Guadalajara Metropolitan Area">Guadalajara</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco (JA)</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">4,796,603</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">12</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="M\xc3\xa9rida, Yucat\xc3\xa1n">M\xc3\xa9rida</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Yucat\xc3\xa1n (YU)</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,283,835</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">19</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Morelia" title="Morelia">Morelia</a></td>\n<td
