style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">20</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Veracruz_(city)" title="Veracruz (city)">Veracruz</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz (VE)</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">891,805</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mexico" title="Religion in Mexico">Religion in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tr style="background:#ddd">\n<th colspan="5"><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mexico" title="Religion in Mexico">Religion in Mexico</a> (2010 census)<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">[2]</a></sup></th>\n</tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="width:100px;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Roman Catholicism</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:blue; width:83%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">83%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other Christian</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:purple; width:10%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">10%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other Religion</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:red; width:0.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">No religion</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:green; width:5%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">5%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Unspecified</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:orange; width:3%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The 2010 census by the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Estad%C3%ADstica_y_Geograf%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Instituto Nacional de Estad\xc3\xadstica y Geograf\xc3\xada">Instituto Nacional de Estad\xc3\xadstica y Geograf\xc3\xada</a> (National Institute of Statistics and Geography) gave <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Mexico">Roman Catholicism</a> as the main religion, with 83% of the population, while 10% (10,924,103) belong to other Christian denominations, including <a href="/wiki/Evangelicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelicals">Evangelicals</a> (5%); <a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> (1.6%); other Protestant or Reformed (0.7%); <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> (1.4%); <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventists</a> (0.6%); and members of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (0.3%).<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">[2]</a></sup> 172,891 (or less than 0.2% of the total) belonged to other, non-Christian religions; 4.7% declared having <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Mexico" title="Irreligion in Mexico">no religion</a>; 2.7% were unspecified.<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG/220px-2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG/330px-2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG/440px-2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2013-12-23_Antigua_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Guadalupe_anagoria.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe">Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe</a> is a major Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/List_of_Christian_pilgrimage_sites" title="List of Christian pilgrimage sites">pilgrimage site</a>, with some twenty million annual visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The 92,924,489<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">[2]</a></sup> Catholics of Mexico constitute in absolute terms the second largest Catholic community in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>\'s.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> 47% percent of them attend church services weekly.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> The feast day of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Our Lady of Guadalupe">Our Lady of Guadalupe</a>, the patron saint of Mexico, is celebrated on December 12 and is regarded by many Mexicans as the most important religious holiday of their country.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The 2010 census reported 314,932 members of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints,<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">[2]</a></sup> though the church in 2009 claimed to have over one million registered members.<sup id="cite_ref-lds-Mexico_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lds-Mexico-294">[294]</a></sup> About 25% of registered members attend a weekly sacrament service although this can fluctuate up and down.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopedia-mormonism_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopedia-mormonism-295">[295]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The presence of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Jews in Mexico">Jews in Mexico</a> dates back to 1521, when Hern\xc3\xa1n Cort\xc3\xa9s conquered the Aztecs, accompanied by several <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">Conversos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> According to the 2010 census, there are 67,476 Jews in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Mexico" title="Islam in Mexico">Islam in Mexico</a> is practiced mostly by <a href="/wiki/Arab_Mexican" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab Mexican">Arab Mexicans</a>, while there is also a small community of Muslims among indigenous Mexicans around the <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_las_Casas" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de las Casas">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de las Casas</a> area in Chiapas.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> In the 2010 census 18,185 Mexicans reported belonging to an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern religion">Eastern religion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">[2]</a></sup> a category which includes a tiny <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Mexico" title="Buddhism in Mexico">Buddhist</a> population.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Mexico" title="Women in Mexico">Women in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Until the twentieth century, Mexico was an overwhelmingly rural country, with rural women\'s status defined within the context of the family and local community. With urbanization beginning in the sixteenth century, following the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec empire">Spanish conquest of the Aztec empire</a>, cities have provided economic and social opportunities not possible within rural villages. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Mexico">Roman Catholicism in Mexico</a> has shaped societal attitudes about women\'s social role, emphasizing the role of women as nurturers of the family, with the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a> as a model. <a href="/wiki/Marianismo" title="Marianismo">Marianismo</a> has been an ideal, with women\'s role as being within the family under the authority of men. In the twentieth century, Mexican women made great strides toward toward a more equal legal and social status. In 1953, women in Mexico were granted the vote in national elections.</p>\n<p>Mexican women face discrimination and at times harassment from the <a href="/wiki/Machismo" title="Machismo">machismo</a> population. Although women in Mexico are making big advancements they are faced with the traditional expectations of being the head of the household. Researcher Margarita Vald\xc3\xa9s noted that while there are few inequalities enforced by law or policy in Mexico, there are gender inequalities perpetuated by social structures and Mexican cultural expectations that limit the capabilities of Mexican women.<sup id="cite_ref-capabilities_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-capabilities-299">[299]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Mexico has the 16th highest rate of homicides committed against women in the world <sup id="cite_ref-femicide_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-femicide-300">[300]</a></sup> The prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a> against women in Mexican marital relationships varies at between 30 and 60 percent of relationships.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-301">[301]</a></sup> The remains of the victims were frequently mutilated.<sup id="cite_ref-hp_8Jan2015_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hp_8Jan2015-302">[302]</a></sup> According to a 1997 study, domestic abuse in Mexican culture "is embedded in gender and marital relations fostered in Mexican women\'s dependence on their spouses for subsistence and for self-esteem, sustained by ideologies of romantic love, by family structure and residential arrangements."<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> The perpetrators are often the boyfriend, father-in-law, ex-husbands or husbands but only 1.6% of the murder cases led to an arrest and sentencing.<sup id="cite_ref-hp_8Jan2015_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hp_8Jan2015-302">[302]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(September 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Mexico" title="Culture of Mexico">Culture of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Diego_riveraa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Diego_riveraa.jpg/200px-Diego_riveraa.jpg" width="200" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Diego_riveraa.jpg/300px-Diego_riveraa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Diego_riveraa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="386" data-file-height="450" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Diego_riveraa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Frida_Kahlo" title="Frida Kahlo">Frida Kahlo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a> in 1932</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexican culture reflects the complexity of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mexico" title="History of Mexico">country\'s history</a> through the blending of indigenous cultures and the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Spain" title="Culture of Spain">culture of Spain</a>, imparted during Spain\'s 300-year colonization of Mexico. Exogenous cultural elements have been incorporated into Mexican culture as time has passed.</p>\n<p>The Porfirian era (<i>el <a href="/wiki/Porfirio_D%C3%ADaz" title="Porfirio D\xc3\xadaz">Porfiriato</a></i>), in the last quarter of the 19th century and the first decade of the 20th century, was marked by economic progress and peace. After four decades of civil unrest and war, Mexico saw the development of philosophy and the arts, promoted by President D\xc3\xadaz himself. Since that time, as accentuated during the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a>, cultural identity has had its foundation in the <i>mestizaje</i>, of which the indigenous (i.e. Amerindian) element is the core. In light of the various ethnicities that formed the Mexican people, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vasconcelos" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos">Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos</a> in his publication <i>La Raza C\xc3\xb3smica</i> (The Cosmic Race) (1925) defined Mexico to be the melting pot of all races (thus extending the definition of the <i>mestizo</i>) not only biologically but culturally as well.<sup id="cite_ref-vasconcelos160_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vasconcelos160-304">[304]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_literature" title="Mexican literature">Mexican literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_literature" title="Mesoamerican literature">Mesoamerican literature</a></div>\n<p>Mexican literature has its antecedents in the literatures of the indigenous settlements of Mesoamerica. The most well known prehispanic poet is <a href="/wiki/Nezahualcoyotl_(tlatoani)" title="Nezahualcoyotl (tlatoani)">Nezahualcoyotl</a>. Modern Mexican literature was influenced by the concepts of the Spanish colonialization of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>. Outstanding colonial writers and poets include <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ruiz_de_Alarc%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ruiz de Alarc\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ruiz de Alarc\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz" title="Juana In\xc3\xa9s de la Cruz">Juana In\xc3\xa9s de la Cruz</a>.</p>\n<p>Other writers include <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Reyes" title="Alfonso Reyes">Alfonso Reyes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Lizardi" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Joaqu\xc3\xadn Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lizardi">Jos\xc3\xa9 Joaqu\xc3\xadn Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lizardi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Manuel_Altamirano" title="Ignacio Manuel Altamirano">Ignacio Manuel Altamirano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Fuentes" title="Carlos Fuentes">Carlos Fuentes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Octavio_Paz" title="Octavio Paz">Octavio Paz</a> (Nobel Laureate), <a href="/wiki/Renato_Leduc" title="Renato Leduc">Renato Leduc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Monsiv%C3%A1is" title="Carlos Monsiv\xc3\xa1is">Carlos Monsiv\xc3\xa1is</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elena_Poniatowska" title="Elena Poniatowska">Elena Poniatowska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Azuela" title="Mariano Azuela">Mariano Azuela</a> ("Los de abajo") and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rulfo" title="Juan Rulfo">Juan Rulfo</a> ("Pedro P\xc3\xa1ramo"). <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Traven" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruno Traven">Bruno Traven</a> wrote "Canasta de cuentos mexicanos" (Mexican tales basket), "El tesoro de la Sierra Madre" (Treasure of the Sierra Madre).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_art" title="Mexican art">Mexican art</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg/250px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg/375px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg/500px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a> is the preeminent arts museum in Mexico.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Post-revolutionary art in Mexico had its expression in the works of renowned artists such as <a href="/wiki/David_Alfaro_Siqueiros" title="David Alfaro Siqueiros">David Alfaro Siqueiros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federico_Cant%C3%BA_Garza" title="Federico Cant\xc3\xba Garza">Federico Cant\xc3\xba Garza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frida_Kahlo" title="Frida Kahlo">Frida Kahlo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_O%27Gorman" title="Juan O\'Gorman">Juan O\'Gorman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Clemente_Orozco" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Clemente Orozco">Jos\xc3\xa9 Clemente Orozco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rufino_Tamayo" title="Rufino Tamayo">Rufino Tamayo</a>. Diego Rivera, the most well-known figure of Mexican muralism, painted the <a href="/wiki/Man_at_the_Crossroads" title="Man at the Crossroads">Man at the Crossroads</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a> in New York City, a huge mural that was destroyed the next year because of the inclusion of a portrait of Russian communist leader <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Lenin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> Some of Rivera\'s murals are displayed at the Mexican <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Mexico)" title="National Palace (Mexico)">National Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palace of Fine Arts</a>.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_architecture" title="Mesoamerican architecture">Mesoamerican architecture</a> is mostly noted for its pyramids which are the largest such structures outside of Ancient Egypt.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_architecture" title="Spanish Colonial architecture">Spanish Colonial architecture</a> is marked by the contrast between the simple, solid construction demanded by the new environment and the Baroque ornamentation exported from Spain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Mexico, as the center of New Spain has some of the most renowned buildings built in this style.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Mexico" title="Cinema of Mexico">Cinema of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg/170px-Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg/255px-Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="340" data-file-height="453" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nActress <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del R\xc3\xado">Dolores del R\xc3\xado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> star in the 1920s and 1930s and prominent figure of the <i><a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Mexican_cinema" title="Golden Age of Mexican cinema">Golden Age of Mexican cinema</a></i> in the 1940s and 1950s</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Mexico" title="Cinema of Mexico">Mexican films</a> from the <i><a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Mexican_cinema" title="Golden Age of Mexican cinema">Golden Age</a></i> in the 1940s and 1950s are the greatest examples of Latin American cinema, with a huge industry comparable to the Hollywood of those years. Mexican films were exported and exhibited in all of Latin America and Europe. <i><a href="/wiki/Maria_Candelaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Candelaria">Maria Candelaria</a></i> (1943) by <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Emilio Fern\xc3\xa1ndez">Emilio Fern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>, was one of the first films awarded a <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d\'Or">Palme d\'Or</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a> in 1946, the first time the event was held after World War II. The famous Spanish-born director <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bu%C3%B1uel" title="Luis Bu\xc3\xb1uel">Luis Bu\xc3\xb1uel</a> realized in Mexico, between 1947 and 1965 some of him master pieces like <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Olvidados" title="Los Olvidados">Los Olvidados</a></i> (1949) and <i><a href="/wiki/Viridiana" title="Viridiana">Viridiana</a></i> (1961). Famous actors and actresses from this period include <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_F%C3%A9lix" title="Mar\xc3\xada F\xc3\xa9lix">Mar\xc3\xada F\xc3\xa9lix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Infante" title="Pedro Infante">Pedro Infante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del R\xc3\xado">Dolores del R\xc3\xado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Negrete" title="Jorge Negrete">Jorge Negrete</a> and the comedian <a href="/wiki/Cantinflas" title="Cantinflas">Cantinflas</a>.</p>\n<p>More recently, films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Like_Water_for_Chocolate_(film)" title="Like Water for Chocolate (film)">Como agua para chocolate</a></i> (1992), <i><a href="/wiki/Cronos_(film)" title="Cronos (film)">Cronos</a></i> (1993), <i><a href="/wiki/Y_tu_mam%C3%A1_tambi%C3%A9n" class="mw-redirect" title="Y tu mam\xc3\xa1 tambi\xc3\xa9n">Y tu mam\xc3\xa1 tambi\xc3\xa9n</a></i> (2001), and <i><a href="/wiki/Pan%27s_Labyrinth" title="Pan\'s Labyrinth">Pan\'s Labyrinth</a></i> (2006) have been successful in creating universal stories about contemporary subjects, and were internationally recognized, as in the prestigious Cannes Film Festival. Mexican directors <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Gonz%C3%A1lez_I%C3%B1%C3%A1rritu" title="Alejandro Gonz\xc3\xa1lez I\xc3\xb1\xc3\xa1rritu">Alejandro Gonz\xc3\xa1lez I\xc3\xb1\xc3\xa1rritu</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Amores_perros" title="Amores perros">Amores perros</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Babel_(film)" title="Babel (film)">Babel</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Birdman_(film)" title="Birdman (film)">Birdman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Revenant_(2015_film)" title="The Revenant (2015 film)">The Revenant</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n">Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_Men" title="Children of Men">Children of Men</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(2013_film)" title="Gravity (2013 film)">Gravity</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_del_Toro" title="Guillermo del Toro">Guillermo del Toro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Carrera" title="Carlos Carrera">Carlos Carrera</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/El_crimen_del_Padre_Amaro" class="mw-redirect" title="El crimen del Padre Amaro">The Crime of Father Amaro</a></i>), screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Arriaga" title="Guillermo Arriaga">Guillermo Arriaga</a> and photographer <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Lubezki" title="Emmanuel Lubezki">Emmanuel Lubezki</a> are some of the most known present-day film makers.</p>\n<p>Some Mexican actors have achieved recognition as Hollywood stars. These include <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Novarro" title="Ramon Novarro">Ramon Novarro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del R\xc3\xado">Dolores del R\xc3\xado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lupe_V%C3%A9lez" title="Lupe V\xc3\xa9lez">Lupe V\xc3\xa9lez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Roland" title="Gilbert Roland">Gilbert Roland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Quinn" title="Anthony Quinn">Anthony Quinn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katy_Jurado" title="Katy Jurado">Katy Jurado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Montalb%C3%A1n" title="Ricardo Montalb\xc3\xa1n">Ricardo Montalb\xc3\xa1n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salma_Hayek" title="Salma Hayek">Salma Hayek</a></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican television">Mexican television</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Mexico" title="List of newspapers in Mexico">List of newspapers in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>There are two major television companies in Mexico that own the four primary networks that broadcast to 75% of the population. They are <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a>, which owns the Canal de las Estrellas and Canal 5 networks, and <a href="/wiki/TV_Azteca" title="TV Azteca">TV Azteca</a>, which owns the Azteca 7 and Azteca Trece networks. Televisa is also the largest producer of Spanish-language content in the world and also the world\'s largest Spanish-language media network.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Multimedios" title="Grupo Multimedios">Grupo Multimedios</a> is another media conglomerate with Spanish-language broadcasting in Mexico, Spain, and the United States. The <i><a href="/wiki/Telenovela" title="Telenovela">telenovelas</a></i> are very traditional in Mexico and are translated to many languages and seen all over the world with renowned names like <a href="/wiki/Ver%C3%B3nica_Castro" title="Ver\xc3\xb3nica Castro">Ver\xc3\xb3nica Castro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A9ndez" title="Luc\xc3\xada M\xc3\xa9ndez">Luc\xc3\xada M\xc3\xa9ndez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thal%C3%ADa" title="Thal\xc3\xada">Thal\xc3\xada</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mexico" title="Music of Mexico">Music of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg/220px-MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg/330px-MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg/440px-MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3248" data-file-height="2403" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MariachiFestivalSanJuanLagos03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMariachi at the Festival del Mariachi, Charrer\xc3\xada y Tequila in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_los_Lagos" title="San Juan de los Lagos">San Juan de los Lagos</a>, Jalisco. Mariachi was inscribed in the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_List" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage List">UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage List</a> in 2011.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexican society enjoys a vast array of music genres, showing the diversity of Mexican culture. Traditional music includes <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">mariachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banda_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Banda music">banda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norte%C3%B1o_(music)" title="Norte\xc3\xb1o (music)">norte\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranchera" title="Ranchera">ranchera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corrido" title="Corrido">corridos</a>; on an everyday basis most Mexicans listen to contemporary music such as <a href="/wiki/Mexican_pop_music" title="Mexican pop music">pop</a>, rock, etc. in both English and Spanish. Mexico has the largest media industry in Latin America, producing Mexican artists who are famous in Central and South America and parts of Europe, especially Spain.</p>\n<p>Some well-known Mexican singers are <a href="/wiki/Thal%C3%ADa" title="Thal\xc3\xada">Thal\xc3\xada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Miguel" title="Luis Miguel">Luis Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gabriel" title="Juan Gabriel">Juan Gabriel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Alejandro Fern\xc3\xa1ndez">Alejandro Fern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julieta_Venegas" title="Julieta Venegas">Julieta Venegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Trevi" title="Gloria Trevi">Gloria Trevi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paulina_Rubio" title="Paulina Rubio">Paulina Rubio</a>. Mexican singers of traditional music are: <a href="/wiki/Lila_Downs" title="Lila Downs">Lila Downs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susana_Harp" title="Susana Harp">Susana Harp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaramar" title="Jaramar">Jaramar</a>, <a href="/wiki/GEO_Meneses" class="mw-redirect" title="GEO Meneses">GEO Meneses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alejandra_Robles" title="Alejandra Robles">Alejandra Robles</a>. Popular groups are <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_Tacuba" title="Caf\xc3\xa9 Tacuba">Caf\xc3\xa9 Tacuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caifanes" title="Caifanes">Caifanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molotov_(band)" title="Molotov (band)">Molotov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Man%C3%A1" title="Man\xc3\xa1">Man\xc3\xa1</a>, among others. Since the early years of the 2000s (decade), <a href="/wiki/Mexican_rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican rock">Mexican rock</a> has seen widespread growth both domestically and internationally.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>According to the Sistema Nacional de Fomento Musical, there are between 120 and 140 youth orchestras affiliated to this federal agency from all federal states.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Some states, through their state agencies in charge of culture and the arts\xe2\x80\x94Ministry or Secretary or Institute or Council of Culture, or in some cases the Secretary of Education or the State University\xe2\x80\x94sponsor the activities of a professional <a href="/wiki/Orchestra" title="Orchestra">symphony orchestra or philharmonic orchestra</a> so all citizens can have access to this artistic expression from the field of classical music. Mexico City is the most intense hub of this activity, hosting 12 professional orchestras sponsored by different agencies such as the National Institute of Fine Arts, the Secretary of Culture of the Federal District, The National University, the National Polytechnic Institute, a Delegaci\xc3\xb3n Pol\xc3\xadtica (Coyoac\xc3\xa1n) and private ventures.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_cuisine" title="Mexican cuisine">Mexican cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG/200px-Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG/300px-Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG/400px-Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i><a href="/wiki/Mole_sauce" title="Mole sauce">Mole sauce</a></i>, which has dozens of varieties across the Republic, is seen as a symbol of <i>Mexicanidad</i><sup id="cite_ref-Mole_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mole-307">[307]</a></sup> and is considered Mexico\'s national dish.<sup id="cite_ref-Mole_307-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mole-307">[307]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile_en_nogada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Chile_en_nogada.jpg/200px-Chile_en_nogada.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Chile_en_nogada.jpg/300px-Chile_en_nogada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Chile_en_nogada.jpg/400px-Chile_en_nogada.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i><a href="/wiki/Chile_en_nogada" class="mw-redirect" title="Chile en nogada">Chile en nogada</a></i>, due to the dish\'s incorporation of red, white and green, is popularly consumed during the celebrations of the<br />\n<i><a href="/wiki/Grito_de_Dolores" class="mw-redirect" title="Grito de Dolores">Grito de Dolores</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n<div style="clear:left"></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexican cuisine is known for its intense and varied flavors, colorful decoration, and variety of spices. Most of today\'s Mexican food is based on pre-Columbian traditions, including Aztec and Maya, combined with culinary trends introduced by Spanish colonists.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadores</a> eventually combined their imported diet of rice, beef, pork, chicken, wine, garlic and onions with the native pre-Columbian food, including maize, tomato, <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guava" title="Guava">guava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chili pepper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(plant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Squash (plant)">squash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a>, peanut, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">turkey</a>.</p>\n<p>Mexican food varies by region, because of local climate and geography and ethnic differences among the indigenous inhabitants and because these different populations were influenced by the Spaniards in varying degrees. The north of Mexico is known for its beef, goat and <a href="/wiki/Ostrich" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostrich">ostrich</a> production and meat dishes, in particular the well-known <a href="/wiki/Arrachera" class="mw-redirect" title="Arrachera">Arrachera</a> cut.</p>\n<p>Central Mexico\'s cuisine is largely made up of influences from the rest of the country, but also has its authentics, such as <a href="/wiki/Barbacoa" title="Barbacoa">barbacoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pozole" title="Pozole">pozole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Menudo_(soup)" title="Menudo (soup)">menudo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamales" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamales">tamales</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carnitas" title="Carnitas">carnitas</a>.</p>\n<p>Southeastern Mexico, on the other hand, is known for its spicy vegetable and chicken-based dishes. The cuisine of Southeastern Mexico also has quite a bit of Caribbean influence, given its geographical location. <a href="/wiki/Veal" title="Veal">Veal</a> is common in the <a href="/wiki/Yucatan" class="mw-redirect" title="Yucatan">Yucatan</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Pork, Turkey, and Fish are preferred by Yucatecos (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Seafood is commonly prepared in the states that border the Pacific Ocean or the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, the latter having a famous reputation for its fish dishes, in particular \xc3\xa0 la veracruzana.</p>\n<p>In modern times, other cuisines of the world have become very popular in Mexico, thus adopting a Mexican fusion. For example, sushi in Mexico is often made with a variety of sauces based on <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tamarind" title="Tamarind">tamarind</a>, and very often served with <a href="/wiki/Serrano_pepper" title="Serrano pepper">serrano</a>-chili-blended soy sauce, or complemented with vinegar, <a href="/wiki/Habanero" title="Habanero">habanero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chipotle" title="Chipotle">chipotle</a> peppers</p>\n<p>The most internationally recognized dishes include chocolate, <a href="/wiki/Taco" title="Taco">tacos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quesadilla" title="Quesadilla">quesadillas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enchilada" title="Enchilada">enchiladas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burrito" title="Burrito">burritos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamale" title="Tamale">tamales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mole_(sauce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mole (sauce)">mole</a> among others. Regional dishes include <a href="/wiki/Mole_(sauce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mole (sauce)">mole poblano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chiles_en_nogada" title="Chiles en nogada">chiles en nogada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chalupa" title="Chalupa">chalupas</a> from <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cabrito" title="Cabrito">cabrito</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machaca" title="Machaca">machaca</a> from Monterrey, <a href="/wiki/Cochinita_pibil" title="Cochinita pibil">cochinita pibil</a> from <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yucat\xc3\xa1n (state)">Yucat\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tlayuda" title="Tlayuda">Tlayudas</a> from <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Barbacoa" title="Barbacoa">barbacoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chilaquiles" title="Chilaquiles">chilaquiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milanesa" title="Milanesa">milanesas</a>, and many others.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Mexico" title="Sport in Mexico">Sport in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Azteca,_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg/220px-Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg/330px-Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg/440px-Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="355" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Azteca,_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Azteca" title="Estadio Azteca">Estadio Azteca</a>, regarded as one of the iconic football stadiums in the world, hosted the 1970 and 1986 World Cup finals and was the main venue of the 1968 Summer Olympics.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Mexico City hosted the <a href="/wiki/1968_Summer_Olympics" title="1968 Summer Olympics">XIX Olympic Games</a> in 1968, making it the first Latin American city to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup> The country has also hosted the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> twice, in <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970</a> and <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Mexico\'s most popular sport is association football. It is commonly believed that football was introduced in Mexico by <a href="/wiki/Cornish_people" title="Cornish people">Cornish</a> miners at the end of the 19th century. By 1902 a five-team league had emerged with a strong British influence.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup> Mexico\'s top clubs are <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club Am\xc3\xa9rica">Am\xc3\xa9rica</a> with 12 championships, <a href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Guadalajara" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Deportivo Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a> with 11, and <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_Toluca_F.C." title="Deportivo Toluca F.C.">Toluca</a> with 10.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Carbajal" title="Antonio Carbajal">Antonio Carbajal</a> was the first player to appear in five World Cups,<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hugo_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Hugo S\xc3\xa1nchez">Hugo S\xc3\xa1nchez</a> was named best <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> player of the 20th century by IFFHS.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg/220px-Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg/330px-Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg/440px-Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1282" data-file-height="814" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_de_beisbol_en_Monterrey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nGame at the <i><a href="/wiki/Estadio_de_B%C3%A9isbol_Monterrey" title="Estadio de B\xc3\xa9isbol Monterrey">Estadio de B\xc3\xa9isbol Monterrey</a></i>. Baseball is most popular in the North (particularly Northwest) and Southeast of Mexico.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Mexican professional baseball league is named the <a href="/wiki/Liga_Mexicana_de_Beisbol" class="mw-redirect" title="Liga Mexicana de Beisbol">Liga Mexicana de Beisbol</a>. While usually not as strong as the United States, the Caribbean countries and Japan, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_baseball_team" title="Mexico national baseball team">Mexico</a> has nonetheless achieved several international baseball titles.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Mexican teams have won the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Series" title="Caribbean Series">Caribbean Series</a> nine times. Mexico has had several players signed by Major League teams, the most famous of them being Dodgers pitcher <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Valenzuela" title="Fernando Valenzuela">Fernando Valenzuela</a>.</p>\n<p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Mexico%27s_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexico\'s basketball team">Mexico\'s basketball team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIBA_Americas_Championship" title="2013 FIBA Americas Championship">Americas Basketball Championship</a> and qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2014_Basketball_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Basketball World Cup">2014 Basketball World Cup</a> where it reached the playoffs. Because of these achievements the country earned the hosting rights for the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIBA_Americas_Championship" title="2015 FIBA Americas Championship">2015 FIBA Americas Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bullfighting" title="Bullfighting">Bullfighting</a> is a popular sport in the country, and almost all large cities have bullrings. <a href="/wiki/Plaza_M%C3%A9xico" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaza M\xc3\xa9xico">Plaza M\xc3\xa9xico</a> in Mexico City, is the largest bullring in the world, which seats 55,000 people. Professional wrestling (or <a href="/wiki/Lucha_libre" title="Lucha libre">Lucha libre</a> in Spanish) is a major crowd draw with national promotions such as <a href="/wiki/Lucha_Libre_AAA_World_Wide" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucha Libre AAA World Wide">AAA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consejo_Mundial_de_Lucha_Libre" title="Consejo Mundial de Lucha Libre">CMLL</a> and others.</p>\n<p>Mexico is an international power in <a href="/wiki/Professional_boxing" title="Professional boxing">professional boxing</a> (at the amateur level, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_at_the_Olympics" title="Mexico at the Olympics">several Olympic boxing medals</a> have also been won by Mexico). <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Saldivar" title="Vicente Saldivar">Vicente Saldivar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Olivares" title="Rub\xc3\xa9n Olivares">Rub\xc3\xa9n Olivares</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Salvador S\xc3\xa1nchez">Salvador S\xc3\xa1nchez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julio_C%C3%A9sar_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Julio C\xc3\xa9sar Ch\xc3\xa1vez">Julio C\xc3\xa9sar Ch\xc3\xa1vez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lopez_Nava" class="mw-redirect" title="Ricardo Lopez Nava">Ricardo Lopez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erik_Morales" class="mw-redirect" title="Erik Morales">Erik Morales</a> are but a few Mexican fighters who have been ranked among the best of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Notable Mexican athletes include golfer <a href="/wiki/Lorena_Ochoa" title="Lorena Ochoa">Lorena Ochoa</a>, who was ranked first in the <a href="/wiki/LPGA" title="LPGA">LPGA</a> world rankings prior to her retirement,<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ana_Guevara" title="Ana Guevara">Ana Guevara</a>, former world champion of the 400 metres (1,300&#160;ft) and Olympic subchampion in Athens 2004, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Platas" title="Fernando Platas">Fernando Platas</a>, four-time Olympic medal winning diver, and taekwondo fighter <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Espinoza" title="Mar\xc3\xada Espinoza">Mar\xc3\xada Espinoza</a>, most decorated Mexican female Olympian.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Mexico" title="Healthcare in Mexico">Healthcare in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Since the early 1990s, Mexico entered a transitional stage in the health of its population and some indicators such as mortality patterns are identical to those found in highly developed countries like Germany or Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> Mexico\'s medical infrastructure is highly rated for the most part and is usually excellent in major cities,<sup id="cite_ref-Health_Care_in_Mexico_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_Care_in_Mexico-320">[320]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> but rural communities still lack equipment for advanced medical procedures, forcing patients in those locations to travel to the closest urban areas to get specialized medical care.<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_117-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Social_determinants_of_health_in_Mexico" title="Social determinants of health in Mexico">Social determinants of health</a> can be used to evaluate the state of health in Mexico.</p>\n<p>State-funded institutions such as <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Social_Security_Institute" title="Mexican Social Security Institute">Mexican Social Security Institute</a> (IMSS) and the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Social_Security_and_Services_for_State_Workers" title="Institute for Social Security and Services for State Workers">Institute for Social Security and Services for State Workers</a> (ISSSTE) play a major role in health and social security. Private health services are also very important and account for 13% of all medical units in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Medical training is done mostly at public universities with much specializations done in vocational or internship settings. Some public universities in Mexico, such as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Guadalajara" title="University of Guadalajara">University of Guadalajara</a>, have signed agreements with the U.S. to receive and train American students in Medicine. Health care costs in private institutions and prescription drugs in Mexico are on average lower than that of its North American economic partners.<sup id="cite_ref-Health_Care_in_Mexico_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_Care_in_Mexico-320">[320]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mexico" title="Education in Mexico">Education in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_Central..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Biblioteca_Central..jpg/220px-Biblioteca_Central..jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Biblioteca_Central..jpg/330px-Biblioteca_Central..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Biblioteca_Central..jpg/440px-Biblioteca_Central..jpg 2x" data-file-width="2557" data-file-height="1910" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_Central..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Central_Library_(UNAM)" title="Central Library (UNAM)">Central Library</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Autonomous_University_of_Mexico" title="National Autonomous University of Mexico">National Autonomous University of Mexico</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 2004, the literacy rate was at 97%<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> for youth under the age of 14 and 91% for people over 15,<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> placing Mexico at the 24th place in the world rank according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Autonomous_University_of_Mexico" title="National Autonomous University of Mexico">National Autonomous University of Mexico</a> ranks 190th place in the Top 200 World University Ranking published by The Times Higher Education Supplement in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> Private business schools also stand out in international rankings. <a href="/wiki/IPADE" class="mw-redirect" title="IPADE">IPADE</a> and <a href="/wiki/EGADE" class="mw-redirect" title="EGADE">EGADE</a>, the business schools of <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Panamericana" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Panamericana">Universidad Panamericana</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Monterrey_Institute_of_Technology_and_Higher_Education" title="Monterrey Institute of Technology and Higher Education">Monterrey Institute of Technology and Higher Education</a> respectively, were ranked in the top 10 in a survey conducted by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> among recruiters outside the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div role="navigation"
